         </div>

       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <b>
        Latvia
       </b>
       , (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
           <span title="'v' in 'vie'">
            v
           </span>
           <span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">
            i
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="nowrap">
         (
         <span class="unicode haudio">
          <span class="fn">
           <span style="white-space:nowrap">
            <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Latvia.ogg" title="About this sound">
             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
            </a>
           </span>
           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9e/En-us-Latvia.ogg" title="En-us-Latvia.ogg">
            listen
           </a>
          </span>
         </span>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">
        Latvian
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="lv">
         Latvija
        </span>
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Latvian" title="Help:IPA/Latvian">
         [ˈlatvija]
        </a>
       </span>
       ), officially the
       <b>
        Republic of Latvia
       </b>
       (Latvian:
       <i>
        <span lang="lv">
         Latvijas Republika
        </span>
       </i>
       ), is a country in the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_region" title="Baltic region">
        Baltic region
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Europe" title="Northern Europe">
        Northern Europe
       </a>
       , one of the three
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">
        Baltic states
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is bordered by
       <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">
        Estonia
       </a>
       to the north,
       <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">
        Lithuania
       </a>
       to the south,
       <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
        Russia
       </a>
       to the east, and
       <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">
        Belarus
       </a>
       to the southeast, as well as sharing a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maritime_border" title="Maritime border">
        maritime border
       </a>
       with
       <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">
        Sweden
       </a>
       to the west. Latvia has 1,957,200 inhabitants
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and a territory of 64,589 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (24,938 sq mi).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Latvia_in_Brief_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Latvia_in_Brief-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The country has a
       <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">
        temperate seasonal climate
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After centuries of
       <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Livonia" title="Swedish Livonia">
        Swedish
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Livonia" title="Duchy of Livonia">
        Livonian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">
        Polish
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">
        Russian rule
       </a>
       , a rule mainly executed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Germans" title="Baltic Germans">
        Baltic German
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Aristocracy" title="Aristocracy">
        aristocracy
       </a>
       , the Republic of Latvia was established on 18 November 1918 after declaring independence from
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">
        Russia
       </a>
       in the aftermath of
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Germanis_2-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Germanis-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, by the 1930s, the country became increasingly autocratic after the
       <a href="/wiki/1934_Latvian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1934 Latvian coup d'état">
        coup in 1934
       </a>
       establishing an authoritarian regime under
       <a href="/wiki/K%C4%81rlis_Ulmanis" title="Kārlis Ulmanis">
        Kārlis Ulmanis
       </a>
       . The country's
       <i>
        de facto
       </i>
       independence was interrupted at the outset of
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       , beginning with Latvia's
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_Latvia_in_1940" title="Soviet occupation of Latvia in 1940">
        forcible incorporation
       </a>
       into the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
        Soviet Union
       </a>
       , followed by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Latvia_by_Nazi_Germany" title="Occupation of Latvia by Nazi Germany">
        invasion and occupation
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
        Nazi Germany
       </a>
       in 1941, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_re-occupation_of_Latvia_in_1944" title="Soviet re-occupation of Latvia in 1944">
        re-occupation by the Soviets
       </a>
       in 1944 to form the
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Latvian Soviet Socialist Republic">
        Latvian SSR
       </a>
       for the next fifty years. The peaceful
       <a href="/wiki/Singing_Revolution" title="Singing Revolution">
        Singing Revolution
       </a>
       , starting in 1987, called for Baltic emancipation from Soviet rule and condemning the "Stalinist" regime's illegal takeover.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It ended with the
       <a href="/wiki/On_the_Restoration_of_Independence_of_the_Republic_of_Latvia" title="On the Restoration of Independence of the Republic of Latvia">
        Declaration on the Restoration of Independence of the Republic of Latvia
       </a>
       on 4 May 1990, and restoring de facto
       <a href="/wiki/State_continuity_of_the_Baltic_states" title="State continuity of the Baltic states">
        independence
       </a>
       on 21 August 1991.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Latvia is a democratic
       <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">
        republic
       </a>
       and a highly developed country
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       . Its capital
       <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">
        Riga
       </a>
       served as the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">
        European Capital of Culture in 2014
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">
        Latvian
       </a>
       is the official language. Latvia is a
       <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">
        unitary state
       </a>
       , divided into 119
       <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Latvia" title="Administrative divisions of Latvia">
        administrative divisions
       </a>
       , of which 110 are municipalities and 9 are cities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Latvians are the indigenous people of Latvia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Latvia_in_Brief_15-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Latvia_in_Brief-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">
        Latvian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_language" title="Lithuanian language">
        Lithuanian
       </a>
       are the only two surviving
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_languages" title="Baltic languages">
        Baltic languages
       </a>
       . Despite foreign rule from the 13th to 20th centuries, the Latvian nation maintained its identity throughout the generations via the language and musical traditions. As a consequence of centuries of Russian rule (1710–1918) and later
       <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Baltic_states" title="Occupation of the Baltic states">
        Soviet occupation
       </a>
       , Latvia is home to a large number of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltic_Russians" title="Baltic Russians">
        ethnic Russians
       </a>
       (26.9% in
       <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_Latvia" title="Russians in Latvia">
        Latvia
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mfa.gov.lv_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mfa.gov.lv-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ), some of whom (14.1% of Latvian residents) have not gained citizenship, leaving them with
       <a href="/wiki/Non-citizens_(Latvia)" title="Non-citizens (Latvia)">
        no citizenship
       </a>
       at all. Until World War II, Latvia also had significant minorities of ethnic
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Germans" title="Baltic Germans">
        Germans
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Latvia" title="History of the Jews in Latvia">
        Jews
       </a>
       . Latvia is historically predominantly
       <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">
        Lutheran
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">
        Protestant
       </a>
       , except for the
       <a href="/wiki/Latgale" title="Latgale">
        Latgale
       </a>
       region in the southeast, which has historically been predominantly
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">
        Roman Catholic
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Russian population has also brought a significant portion of
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">
        Eastern Orthodox
       </a>
       Christians.
      </p>
      <p>
       It is a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">
        NATO
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">
        Council of Europe
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Baltic_Sea_States" title="Council of the Baltic Sea States">
        CBSS
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">
        IMF
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NB8" title="NB8">
        NB8
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Investment_Bank" title="Nordic Investment Bank">
        NIB
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">
        OECD
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">
        OSCE
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">
        WTO
       </a>
       . For 2014, Latvia was listed 46th on the
       <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">
        Human Development Index
       </a>
       and as a
       <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">
        high income country
       </a>
       on 1 July 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A full member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">
        Eurozone
       </a>
       , it uses the
       <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">
        euro
       </a>
       as its currency since 1 January 2014, replacing the
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_lats" title="Latvian lats">
        Latvian lats
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
        Etymology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The name
       <i>
        Latvija
       </i>
       is derived from the name of the ancient
       <a href="/wiki/Latgalians" title="Latgalians">
        Latgalians
       </a>
       , one of four
       <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-Europeans" title="Proto-Indo-Europeans">
        Indo-European
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Balts" title="Balts">
        Baltic tribes
       </a>
       (along with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Couronians" title="Couronians">
        Couronians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Selonians" title="Selonians">
        Selonians
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Semigallians" title="Semigallians">
        Semigallians
       </a>
       ), which formed the ethnic core of modern
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latvian_people" title="Latvian people">
        Latvians
       </a>
       together with the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Finns" title="Baltic Finns">
        Finnic
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Livonian_people" title="Livonian people">
        Livonians
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Henry_of_Latvia" title="Henry of Latvia">
        Henry of Latvia
       </a>
       coined the
       <a href="/wiki/Latinisation_of_names" title="Latinisation of names">
        latinisations
       </a>
       of the country's name, "Lettigallia" and "Lethia", both derived from the Latgalians. The terms inspired the variations on the country's name in
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance languages
       </a>
       from "Letonia" and in several
       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">
        Germanic languages
       </a>
       from "Lettland".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Latvia" title="History of Latvia">
        History of Latvia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Around 3000 BC, the proto-Baltic ancestors of the Latvian people settled on the eastern coast of the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">
        Baltic Sea
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Balts" title="Balts">
        Balts
       </a>
       established trade routes to Rome and
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantium" title="Byzantium">
        Byzantium
       </a>
       , trading local
       <a href="/wiki/Amber" title="Amber">
        amber
       </a>
       for precious metals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By 900 AD, four distinct Baltic tribes inhabited Latvia:
       <a href="/wiki/Curonians" title="Curonians">
        Curonians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latgalians" title="Latgalians">
        Latgalians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Selonians" title="Selonians">
        Selonians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Semigallians" title="Semigallians">
        Semigallians
       </a>
       (in Latvian:
       <i>
        kurši
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        latgaļi
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        sēļi
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        zemgaļi
       </i>
       ), as well as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Livonian_people" title="Livonian people">
        Livonians
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        lībieši
       </i>
       ) speaking a Finnic language.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 12th century in the territory of Latvia, there were 14 lands with their rulers:
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Vanema&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Vanema (page does not exist)">
        Vanema
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ventava&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ventava (page does not exist)">
        Ventava
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bandava" title="Bandava">
        Bandava
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Piemare" title="Piemare">
        Piemare
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Duvzare&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Duvzare (page does not exist)">
        Duvzare
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ceklis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ceklis (page does not exist)">
        Ceklis
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Megava&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Megava (page does not exist)">
        Megava
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pils%C4%81ts&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pilsāts (page does not exist)">
        Pilsāts
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Upmale&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Upmale (page does not exist)">
        Upmale
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=S%C4%93lija(land)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sēlija(land) (page does not exist)">
        Sēlija
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Koknese(land)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Koknese(land) (page does not exist)">
        Koknese
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jersika" title="Jersika">
        Jersika
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/T%C4%81lava" title="Tālava">
        Tālava
       </a>
       and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Adzele&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Adzele (page does not exist)">
        Adzele
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Medieval_period">
        The Medieval period
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The Medieval period">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Terra_Mariana" title="Terra Mariana">
        Terra Mariana
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Livonian_Crusade" title="Livonian Crusade">
        Livonian Crusade
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Crusades" title="Northern Crusades">
        Northern Crusades
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Medieval_Livonia_1260.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1034" data-file-width="955" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Medieval_Livonia_1260.svg/220px-Medieval_Livonia_1260.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Medieval_Livonia_1260.svg/330px-Medieval_Livonia_1260.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Medieval_Livonia_1260.svg/440px-Medieval_Livonia_1260.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Medieval_Livonia_1260.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Terra_Mariana" title="Terra Mariana">
          Terra Mariana
         </a>
         , medieval Livonia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Burg_Turaida04.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2665" data-file-width="3570" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Burg_Turaida04.jpg/220px-Burg_Turaida04.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Burg_Turaida04.jpg/330px-Burg_Turaida04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Burg_Turaida04.jpg/440px-Burg_Turaida04.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Burg_Turaida04.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Turaida_Castle" title="Turaida Castle">
          Turaida Castle
         </a>
         near
         <a href="/wiki/Sigulda" title="Sigulda">
          Sigulda
         </a>
         , built in 1214 under
         <a href="/wiki/Albert_of_Riga" title="Albert of Riga">
          Albert of Riga
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Haupthandelsroute_Hanse.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="603" data-file-width="789" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Haupthandelsroute_Hanse.png/220px-Haupthandelsroute_Hanse.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Haupthandelsroute_Hanse.png/330px-Haupthandelsroute_Hanse.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Haupthandelsroute_Hanse.png/440px-Haupthandelsroute_Hanse.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Haupthandelsroute_Hanse.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         In 1282,
         <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">
          Riga
         </a>
         became a member of the
         <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">
          Hanseatic League
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Although the local people had contact with the outside world for centuries, they became more fully integrated into the European socio-political system in the 12th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first missionaries, sent by the Pope, sailed up the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daugava_River" title="Daugava River">
        Daugava River
       </a>
       in the late 12th century, seeking converts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lonely_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lonely-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The local people, however, did not convert to Christianity as readily as the Church had hoped.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lonely_31-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lonely-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teutonic_Knights" title="Teutonic Knights">
        German crusaders
       </a>
       were sent, or more likely decided to go on their own accord as they were known to do in search of pagans to kill and loot throughout eastern Europe.
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Meinhard" title="Saint Meinhard">
        Saint Meinhard of Segeberg
       </a>
       arrived in Ikšķile, in 1184, traveling with merchants to Livonia, on a Catholic mission to convert the population from their original
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pagan" title="Pagan">
        pagan
       </a>
       beliefs. Pope Celestine III had called for
       <a href="/wiki/Livonian_Crusade#Wars_against_Estonians_(1208–27)" title="Livonian Crusade">
        a crusade against pagans in Northern Europe
       </a>
       in 1193. When peaceful means of conversion failed to produce results, Meinhard plotted to convert Livonians by force of arms.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the beginning of the 13th century, Germans ruled large parts of today's Latvia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lonely_31-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lonely-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Together with Southern Estonia, these conquered areas formed the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crusader_state" title="Crusader state">
        crusader state
       </a>
       that became known as
       <a href="/wiki/Terra_Mariana" title="Terra Mariana">
        Terra Mariana
       </a>
       or Livonia. In 1282, Riga, and later the cities of
       <a href="/wiki/C%C4%93sis" title="Cēsis">
        Cēsis
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Limba%C5%BEi" title="Limbaži">
        Limbaži
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Koknese" title="Koknese">
        Koknese
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Valmiera" title="Valmiera">
        Valmiera
       </a>
       , became part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">
        Hanseatic League
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lonely_31-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lonely-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Riga became an important point of east-west trading
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lonely_31-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lonely-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and formed close cultural links with
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">
        Western Europe
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Reformation_period_and_Polish-Lithuanian_rule">
        The Reformation period and Polish-Lithuanian rule
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The Reformation period and Polish-Lithuanian rule">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Livonia" title="Swedish Livonia">
        Swedish Livonia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Courland_and_Semigallia" title="Duchy of Courland and Semigallia">
        Duchy of Courland and Semigallia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Livonia" title="Duchy of Livonia">
        Duchy of Livonia
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">
        Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Swedish_Empire_(1560-1815)_en2.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2213" data-file-width="1802" height="270" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Swedish_Empire_%281560-1815%29_en2.png/220px-Swedish_Empire_%281560-1815%29_en2.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Swedish_Empire_%281560-1815%29_en2.png/330px-Swedish_Empire_%281560-1815%29_en2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Swedish_Empire_%281560-1815%29_en2.png/440px-Swedish_Empire_%281560-1815%29_en2.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Swedish_Empire_(1560-1815)_en2.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Empire" title="Swedish Empire">
          Swedish Empire
         </a>
         (1560–1815).
         <br/>
         Riga became the capital of
         <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Livonia" title="Swedish Livonia">
          Swedish Livonia
         </a>
         and the largest city in the Swedish Empire.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After the
       <a href="/wiki/Livonian_War" title="Livonian War">
        Livonian War
       </a>
       (1558–1583), Livonia (Latvia) fell under
       <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">
        Polish and Lithuanian
       </a>
       rule.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lonely_31-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lonely-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The southern part of Estonia and the northern part of Latvia were ceded to the
       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">
        Grand Duchy of Lithuania
       </a>
       and formed into the
       <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Livonia" title="Duchy of Livonia">
        Duchy of Livonia
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Ducatus Livoniae Ultradunensis
       </i>
       ).
       <a href="/wiki/Gotthard_Kettler" title="Gotthard Kettler">
        Gotthard Kettler
       </a>
       , the last Master of the
       <a href="/wiki/Livonian_Order" title="Livonian Order">
        Order of Livonia
       </a>
       , formed the
       <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Courland_and_Semigallia" title="Duchy of Courland and Semigallia">
        Duchy of Courland and Semigallia
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Though the duchy was a vassal state to Poland, it retained a considerable degree of autonomy and experienced a golden age in the 16th century.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latgalia" title="Latgalia">
        Latgalia
       </a>
       , the easternmost region of Latvia, became a part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Inflanty_Voivodeship" title="Inflanty Voivodeship">
        Inflanty Voivodeship
       </a>
       of the Polish-Lithuanian Commonwealth.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 17th and early 18th centuries, the Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth,
       <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Empire" title="Swedish Empire">
        Sweden
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">
        Russia
       </a>
       struggled for supremacy in the eastern Baltic. After the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Swedish_War_(1600%E2%80%931611)" title="Polish–Swedish War (1600–1611)">
        Polish–Swedish War
       </a>
       , northern Livonia (including Vidzeme) came under Swedish rule. Riga became the capital of
       <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Livonia" title="Swedish Livonia">
        Swedish Livonia
       </a>
       and the largest city in the entire Swedish Empire.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Fighting continued sporadically between Sweden and Poland until the
       <a href="/wiki/Truce_of_Altmark" title="Truce of Altmark">
        Truce of Altmark
       </a>
       in 1629.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       In Latvia, the Swedish period is generally remembered as positive;
       <a href="/wiki/Serfdom" title="Serfdom">
        serfdom
       </a>
       was eased, a network of schools was established for the peasantry, and the power of the regional
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Germans" title="Baltic Germans">
        barons
       </a>
       was diminished.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Several important cultural changes occurred during this time. Under Swedish and largely German rule, western Latvia adopted
       <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">
        Lutheranism
       </a>
       as its main religion. The ancient tribes of the Couronians, Semigallians, Selonians, Livs, and northern Latgallians assimilated to form the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latvian_people" title="Latvian people">
        Latvian people
       </a>
       , speaking one
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">
        Latvian language
       </a>
       . Throughout all the centuries, however, an actual Latvian state had not been established, so the borders and definitions of who exactly fell within that group are largely subjective. Meanwhile, largely isolated from the rest of Latvia, southern Latgallians adopted
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">
        Catholicism
       </a>
       under Polish/
       <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">
        Jesuit
       </a>
       influence. The native dialect remained distinct, although it acquired many Polish and Russian loanwords.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Latvia_in_the_Russian_Empire_.281795.E2.80.931917.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Latvia_in_the_Russian_Empire_(1795–1917)">
        Latvia in the Russian Empire (1795–1917)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Latvia in the Russian Empire (1795–1917)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Capitulation_of_Estonia_and_Livonia" title="Capitulation of Estonia and Livonia">
        capitulation of Estonia and Livonia
       </a>
       in 1710 and the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nystad" title="Treaty of Nystad">
        Treaty of Nystad
       </a>
       , ending the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_War" title="Great Northern War">
        Great Northern War
       </a>
       in 1721, gave Vidzeme to Russia (it became part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Governorate_of_Livonia" title="Governorate of Livonia">
        Riga Governorate
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The Latgale region remained part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">
        Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/Inflanty_Voivodeship" title="Inflanty Voivodeship">
        Inflanty Voivodeship
       </a>
       until 1772, when it was incorporated into Russia. The
       <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Courland_and_Semigallia" title="Duchy of Courland and Semigallia">
        Duchy of Courland and Semigallia
       </a>
       became an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_area" title="Autonomous area">
        autonomous
       </a>
       Russian province (the
       <a href="/wiki/Courland_Governorate" title="Courland Governorate">
        Courland Governorate
       </a>
       ) in 1795, bringing all of what is now Latvia into the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">
        Russian Empire
       </a>
       . All three Baltic provinces preserved local laws, German as the local
       <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">
        official language
       </a>
       and their own parliament, the
       <a href="/wiki/Landtag" title="Landtag">
        Landtag
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_War" title="Great Northern War">
        Great Northern War
       </a>
       (1700–1721), up to 40 percent of Latvians died from famine and plague.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Half the residents of Riga were killed by
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_War_plague_outbreak" title="Great Northern War plague outbreak">
        plague in 1710–1711
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The emancipation of the serfs took place in Courland in 1817 and in Vidzeme in 1819.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       In practice, however, the emancipation was actually advantageous to the landowners and nobility,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       as it dispossessed peasants of their land without compensation, forcing them to return to work at the estates "of their own free will".
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the 19th century, the social structure changed dramatically.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       A class of independent farmers established itself after reforms allowed the peasants to repurchase their land, but many landless peasants remained.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       There also developed a growing urban
       <a href="/wiki/Proletariat" title="Proletariat">
        proletariat
       </a>
       and an increasingly influential Latvian
       <a href="/wiki/Bourgeoisie" title="Bourgeoisie">
        bourgeoisie
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Young_Latvians" title="Young Latvians">
        Young Latvian
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">
        Latvian
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="lv">
         Jaunlatvieši
        </span>
       </i>
       ) movement laid the groundwork for nationalism from the middle of the century, many of its leaders looking to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavophile" title="Slavophile">
        Slavophiles
       </a>
       for support against the prevailing German-dominated social order.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The rise in use of the Latvian language in literature and society became known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_National_Awakening" title="Latvian National Awakening">
        First National Awakening
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Russification" title="Russification">
        Russification
       </a>
       began in Latgale after the Polish led the
       <a href="/wiki/January_Uprising" title="January Uprising">
        January Uprising
       </a>
       in 1863: this spread to the rest of what is now Latvia by the 1880s.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The Young Latvians were largely eclipsed by the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Current" title="New Current">
        New Current
       </a>
       , a broad leftist social and political movement, in the 1890s. Popular discontent exploded in the
       <a href="/wiki/1905_Russian_Revolution" title="1905 Russian Revolution">
        1905 Russian Revolution
       </a>
       , which took a nationalist character in the Baltic provinces.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During these two centuries Latvia experienced economic and construction boom – ports were expanded (Riga became the largest port in the Russian Empire), railways built; new factories, banks, and a University were established; many residential, public (theatres and museums), and school buildings were erected; new parks formed; and so on. Riga's boulevards and some streets outside the Old Town date from this period.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Worth mentioning is the fact that
       <a href="/wiki/Numeracy" title="Numeracy">
        numeracy
       </a>
       was also higher in the Estonian and Latvian parts of the Russian Empire, which may have been influenced by the Protestant religion of the inhabitants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Declaration_of_independence">
        Declaration of independence
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Declaration of independence">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Karlis_Ulmanis.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="824" data-file-width="657" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Karlis_Ulmanis.jpg/170px-Karlis_Ulmanis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Karlis_Ulmanis.jpg/255px-Karlis_Ulmanis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Karlis_Ulmanis.jpg/340px-Karlis_Ulmanis.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Karlis_Ulmanis.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/K%C4%81rlis_Ulmanis" title="Kārlis Ulmanis">
          Kārlis Ulmanis
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       devastated the territory of what became the state of Latvia, and other western parts of the Russian Empire. Demands for
       <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">
        self-determination
       </a>
       were initially confined to
       <a href="/wiki/Autonomy" title="Autonomy">
        autonomy
       </a>
       , until a power vacuum was created by the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">
        Russian Revolution
       </a>
       in 1917, followed by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk_(Russia%E2%80%93Central_Powers)" title="Treaty of Brest-Litovsk (Russia–Central Powers)">
        Treaty of Brest-Litovsk
       </a>
       between Russia and Germany in March 1918, then the
       <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">
        Allied
       </a>
       armistice with Germany on 11 November 1918. On 18 November 1918, in Riga, the
       <a href="/wiki/Tautas_padome" title="Tautas padome">
        People's Council of Latvia
       </a>
       proclaimed the independence of the new country, with
       <a href="/wiki/K%C4%81rlis_Ulmanis" title="Kārlis Ulmanis">
        Kārlis Ulmanis
       </a>
       becoming the head of the
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Provisional_Government" title="Latvian Provisional Government">
        provisional government
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_War_of_Independence" title="Latvian War of Independence">
        war of independence
       </a>
       that followed was part of a general chaotic period of civil and new border wars in Eastern Europe. By the spring of 1919, there were actually three governments—Ulmanis's government; the
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Socialist_Soviet_Republic" title="Latvian Socialist Soviet Republic">
        Latvian Soviet government
       </a>
       led by
       <a href="/wiki/P%C4%93teris_Stu%C4%8Dka" title="Pēteris Stučka">
        Pēteris Stučka
       </a>
       , whose forces, supported by the
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">
        Red Army
       </a>
       , occupied almost all of the country; and the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Germans" title="Baltic Germans">
        Baltic German
       </a>
       government of the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Baltic_Duchy" title="United Baltic Duchy">
        United Baltic Duchy
       </a>
       , headed by
       <a href="/wiki/Andrievs_Niedra" title="Andrievs Niedra">
        Andrievs Niedra
       </a>
       and supported by the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltische_Landeswehr" title="Baltische Landeswehr">
        Baltische Landeswehr
       </a>
       and the German
       <a href="/wiki/Freikorps" title="Freikorps">
        Freikorps
       </a>
       unit
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Iron_Division&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Iron Division (page does not exist)">
         Iron Division
        </a>
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Estonian and Latvian forces
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2010)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       defeated the Germans at the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_C%C4%93sis_(1919)" title="Battle of Cēsis (1919)">
        Battle of Wenden
       </a>
       in June 1919, and a massive attack by a predominantly German force—the
       <a href="/wiki/West_Russian_Volunteer_Army" title="West Russian Volunteer Army">
        West Russian Volunteer Army
       </a>
       —under
       <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Bermondt-Avalov" title="Pavel Bermondt-Avalov">
        Pavel Bermondt-Avalov
       </a>
       was repelled in November. Eastern Latvia was cleared of Red Army forces by Latvian and Polish troops in early 1920 (from the Polish perspective the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Daugavpils" title="Battle of Daugavpils">
        Battle of Daugavpils
       </a>
       was a part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Soviet_War" title="Polish–Soviet War">
        Polish–Soviet War
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A freely elected
       <a href="/wiki/Constituent_assembly" title="Constituent assembly">
        Constituent assembly
       </a>
       convened on 1 May 1920, and adopted a liberal constitution, the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Latvia" title="Constitution of Latvia">
         Satversme
        </a>
       </i>
       , in February 1922.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The constitution was partly suspended by Kārlis Ulmanis after his coup in 1934 but reaffirmed in 1990. Since then, it has been amended and is still in effect in Latvia today. With most of Latvia's industrial base evacuated to the interior of Russia in 1915, radical
       <a href="/wiki/Land_reform" title="Land reform">
        land reform
       </a>
       was the central political question for the young state. In 1897, 61.2% of the rural population had been landless; by 1936, that percentage had been reduced to 18%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       By 1923, the extent of cultivated land surpassed the pre-war level. Innovation and rising productivity led to rapid growth of the economy, but it soon suffered from the effects of the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">
        Great Depression
       </a>
       . Latvia showed signs of economic recovery, and the electorate had steadily moved toward the centre during the parliamentary period.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       On 15 May 1934, Ulmanis staged a bloodless
       <a href="/wiki/1934_Latvian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1934 Latvian coup d'état">
        coup
       </a>
       , establishing a nationalist dictatorship that lasted until 1940.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Country_profile_44-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Country_profile-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After 1934, Ulmanis established government corporations to buy up private firms with the aim of "Latvianising" the economy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Latvia_in_World_War_II">
        Latvia in World War II
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Latvia in World War II">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_Latvia_in_1940" title="Soviet occupation of Latvia in 1940">
        Soviet occupation of Latvia in 1940
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Latvia_during_World_War_II" title="German occupation of Latvia during World War II">
        German occupation of Latvia during World War II
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust_in_Latvia" title="The Holocaust in Latvia">
        The Holocaust in Latvia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_partisans" title="Latvian partisans">
        Latvian partisans
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_anti-Nazi_resistance_movement_1941%E2%80%9345" title="Latvian anti-Nazi resistance movement 1941–45">
        Latvian anti-Nazi resistance movement 1941–45
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Riga_1940_Soviet_Army.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="566" data-file-width="900" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Riga_1940_Soviet_Army.jpg/220px-Riga_1940_Soviet_Army.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Riga_1940_Soviet_Army.jpg/330px-Riga_1940_Soviet_Army.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Riga_1940_Soviet_Army.jpg/440px-Riga_1940_Soviet_Army.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Riga_1940_Soviet_Army.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">
          Red Army
         </a>
         troops enter
         <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">
          Riga
         </a>
         (1940).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Early in the morning of 24 August 1939, the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
        Soviet Union
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
        Nazi Germany
       </a>
       signed a 10-year non-aggression pact, called the
       <a href="/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact">
        Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact
       </a>
       . The pact contained a secret protocol, revealed only after Germany's defeat in 1945, according to which the states of Northern and Eastern Europe were divided into German and Soviet "
       <a href="/wiki/Sphere_of_influence" title="Sphere of influence">
        spheres of influence
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mrtext_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mrtext-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the north, Latvia,
       <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">
        Finland
       </a>
       and Estonia were assigned to the Soviet sphere.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mrtext_46-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-mrtext-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A week later, on 1 September 1939, Germany and on 17 September, the Soviet Union
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Poland" title="Soviet invasion of Poland">
        invaded Poland
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBBG_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-PBBG-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         32
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After the conclusion of the Molotov-Ribbentrop Pact, most of the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Germans" title="Baltic Germans">
        Baltic Germans
       </a>
       left Latvia by agreement between Ulmanis' government and Nazi Germany under the
       <a href="/wiki/Heim_ins_Reich" title="Heim ins Reich">
        Heim ins Reich
       </a>
       programme.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Latvia_in_WWII_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Latvia_in_WWII-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In total 50,000 Baltic Germans left by the deadline of December 1939, with 1,600 remaining to conclude business and 13,000 choosing to remain in Latvia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Latvia_in_WWII_48-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Latvia_in_WWII-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most of those who remained left for Germany in summer 1940, when a second resettlement scheme was agreed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The racially approved being resettled mainly in Poland, being given land and businesses in exchange for the money they had received from the sale of their previous assets.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBBG_47-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-PBBG-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         46
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <br/>
       On 5 October 1939, Latvia was forced to accept a "mutual assistance" pact with the Soviet Union, granting the Soviets the right to station between 25,000 and 30,000 troops on Latvian territory.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       State administrators were liquidated and replaced by Soviet cadres.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wettig20_51-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-wettig20-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Elections were held with single pro-Soviet candidates listed for many positions. The resulting people's assembly immediately requested admission into the USSR, which the Soviet Union granted.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wettig20_51-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-wettig20-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Latvia, then a puppet government, was headed by
       <a href="/wiki/Augusts_Kirhen%C5%A1teins" title="Augusts Kirhenšteins">
        Augusts Kirhenšteins
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Soviet Union incorporated Latvia on 5 August 1940, as The
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Latvian Soviet Socialist Republic">
         Latvian Soviet Socialist Republic
        </a>
        .
       </i>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-L19397,_Lettland,_Riga,_Begr%C3%BC%C3%9Fung_der_deutschen_Soldaten.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="800" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-L19397%2C_Lettland%2C_Riga%2C_Begr%C3%BC%C3%9Fung_der_deutschen_Soldaten.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-L19397%2C_Lettland%2C_Riga%2C_Begr%C3%BC%C3%9Fung_der_deutschen_Soldaten.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-L19397%2C_Lettland%2C_Riga%2C_Begr%C3%BC%C3%9Fung_der_deutschen_Soldaten.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-L19397%2C_Lettland%2C_Riga%2C_Begr%C3%BC%C3%9Fung_der_deutschen_Soldaten.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-L19397%2C_Lettland%2C_Riga%2C_Begr%C3%BC%C3%9Fung_der_deutschen_Soldaten.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-L19397%2C_Lettland%2C_Riga%2C_Begr%C3%BC%C3%9Fung_der_deutschen_Soldaten.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-L19397,_Lettland,_Riga,_Begr%C3%BC%C3%9Fung_der_deutschen_Soldaten.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         German soldiers enter Riga, July 1941
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Soviets dealt harshly with their
       <a href="/wiki/Enemy_of_the_people" title="Enemy of the people">
        opponents
       </a>
       – prior to
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">
        Operation Barbarossa
       </a>
       , in less than a year, at least 34,250 Latvians were deported or killed.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most were deported to Siberia where deaths were estimated at 40 percent, officers of the Latvian army being shot on the spot.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBBG_47-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-PBBG-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         48
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 22 June 1941 German troops attacked Soviet forces in Operation Barbarossa. There were some spontaneous uprisings by Latvians against the Red Army which helped the Germans. By 29 June
       <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">
        Riga
       </a>
       was reached and with Soviet troops killed, captured or retreating, Latvia was left under the control of German forces by early July.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBBG_47-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-PBBG-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         78–96
        </span>
       </sup>
       The occupation was followed immediately by SS
       <a href="/wiki/Einsatzgruppen" title="Einsatzgruppen">
        Einsatzgruppen
       </a>
       troops who were to act in accordance with the Nazi
       <a href="/wiki/Generalplan_Ost" title="Generalplan Ost">
        Generalplan Ost
       </a>
       which required the population of Latvia to be cut by 50 percent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBBG_47-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-PBBG-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         64
        </span>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBBG_47-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-PBBG-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         56
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Under German occupation, Latvia was administered as part of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Reichskommissariat_Ostland" title="Reichskommissariat Ostland">
         Reichskommissariat Ostland
        </a>
       </i>
       . Latvian paramilitary and
       <a href="/wiki/Arajs_Kommando" title="Arajs Kommando">
        Auxiliary Police
       </a>
       units established by the occupation authority participated in
       <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">
        the Holocaust
       </a>
       and other atrocities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Country_profile_44-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Country_profile-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       30,000 Jews were shot in Latvia in the autumn of 1941.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBBG_47-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-PBBG-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         127
        </span>
       </sup>
       Another 30,000 Jews from the Riga ghetto were killed in the Rumbula Forest in November and December 1941, to reduce overpopulating in the ghetto and make room for more Jews being brought in from Germany and the West.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBBG_47-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-PBBG-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         128
        </span>
       </sup>
       There was a pause in fighting, apart from partisan activity, until after the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Leningrad" title="Battle of Leningrad">
        siege of Leningrad
       </a>
       ended in January 1944 and the Soviet troops advanced, entering Latvia in July and eventually capturing Riga on 13 October 1944.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBBG_47-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-PBBG-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         271
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       More than 200,000 Latvian citizens died during World War II, including approximately 75,000 Latvian
       <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">
        Jews
       </a>
       murdered during the Nazi occupation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Country_profile_44-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Country_profile-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Latvian soldiers fought on both sides of the conflict, mainly on the German side, with 140,000 men in the
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Legion" title="Latvian Legion">
        Latvian Legion
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Waffen-SS" title="Waffen-SS">
        Waffen-SS
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/308th_Rifle_Division_(Soviet_Union)" title="308th Rifle Division (Soviet Union)">
        308th Latvian Rifle Division
       </a>
       was formed by the Red Army in 1944. On occasions, especially in 1944, opposing Latvian troops faced each other in battle.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBBG_47-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-PBBG-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         299
        </span>
       </sup>
       Activity reaching a peak in late 1946.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBBG_47-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-PBBG-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         326
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Soviet_era_.281940.E2.80.9341.2C_1944.E2.80.9391.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_era_(1940–41,_1944–91)">
        Soviet era (1940–41, 1944–91)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Soviet era (1940–41, 1944–91)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Latvia_by_Soviet_Union_1944%E2%80%931945" title="Occupation of Latvia by Soviet Union 1944–1945">
        Occupation of Latvia by Soviet Union 1944–1945
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Latvian Soviet Socialist Republic">
        Latvian Soviet Socialist Republic
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Stalinism" title="Stalinism">
        Stalinism
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Liepaja_December_1941_massacres_01.jpeg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="319" data-file-width="480" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Liepaja_December_1941_massacres_01.jpeg/220px-Liepaja_December_1941_massacres_01.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Liepaja_December_1941_massacres_01.jpeg/330px-Liepaja_December_1941_massacres_01.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Liepaja_December_1941_massacres_01.jpeg/440px-Liepaja_December_1941_massacres_01.jpeg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Liepaja_December_1941_massacres_01.jpeg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Latvian-Jewish women and children photographed before
         <a href="/wiki/Liep%C4%81ja_massacres" title="Liepāja massacres">
          being murdered at Liepaja
         </a>
         in December 1941.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1944, when Soviet military advances reached Latvia, heavy fighting took place in Latvia between German and Soviet troops, which ended in another German defeat. In the course of the war, both occupying forces conscripted Latvians into their armies, in this way increasing the loss of the nation's "live resources". In 1944, part of the Latvian territory once more came under Soviet control. The Soviets immediately began to reinstate the Soviet system. After the German surrender, it became clear that Soviet forces were there to stay, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latvian_national_partisans" title="Latvian national partisans">
        Latvian national partisans
       </a>
       , soon joined by German collaborators, began to fight against the new occupier.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Anywhere from 120,000 to as many as 300,000 Latvians took refuge from the Soviet army by fleeing to Germany and Sweden.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most sources count 200,000 to 250,000 refugees leaving Latvia, with perhaps as many as 80,000 to 100,000 of them recaptured by the Soviets or, during few months immediately after the end of war,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       returned by the West.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Soviets reoccupied the country in 1944–45, and further deportations followed as the country was
       <a href="/wiki/Collectivization_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Collectivization in the Soviet Union">
        collectivised
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sovietisation" title="Sovietisation">
        Sovieticised
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Country_profile_44-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Country_profile-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 25 March 1949, 43,000 rural residents ("
       <a href="/wiki/Kulak" title="Kulak">
        kulaks
       </a>
       ") and Latvian patriots ("nationalists") were deported to Siberia in a sweeping
       <a href="/wiki/Operation_Priboi" title="Operation Priboi">
        Operation Priboi
       </a>
       in all three
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">
        Baltic states
       </a>
       , which was carefully planned and approved in Moscow already on 29 January 1949.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This operation had the desired effect of reducing the anti Soviet partisan activity.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBBG_47-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-PBBG-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         326
        </span>
       </sup>
       Between 136,000 and 190,000 Latvians, depending on the sources, were imprisoned or deported to Soviet concentration camps (the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulag" title="Gulag">
        Gulag
       </a>
       ) in the post war years, from 1945 to 1952.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some managed to escape arrest and joined the partisans.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
