        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shack_from_Gulag_-_Museum_of_the_Occupation_of_Latvia.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Shack_from_Gulag_-_Museum_of_the_Occupation_of_Latvia.JPG/220px-Shack_from_Gulag_-_Museum_of_the_Occupation_of_Latvia.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Shack_from_Gulag_-_Museum_of_the_Occupation_of_Latvia.JPG/330px-Shack_from_Gulag_-_Museum_of_the_Occupation_of_Latvia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Shack_from_Gulag_-_Museum_of_the_Occupation_of_Latvia.JPG/440px-Shack_from_Gulag_-_Museum_of_the_Occupation_of_Latvia.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shack_from_Gulag_-_Museum_of_the_Occupation_of_Latvia.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Reconstruction of a
         <a href="/wiki/Gulag" title="Gulag">
          Gulag
         </a>
         shack in the
         <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_Occupation_of_Latvia" title="Museum of the Occupation of Latvia">
          Museum of the Occupation of Latvia
         </a>
         , Riga
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the post-war period, Latvia was made to adopt Soviet farming methods. Rural areas were forced into
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Collectivisation" title="Collectivisation">
        collectivisation
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       An extensive programme to impose
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilingualism" title="Bilingualism">
        bilingualism
       </a>
       was initiated in Latvia, limiting the use of Latvian language in official uses in favour of using Russian as the main language. All of the minority schools (Jewish, Polish, Belarusian, Estonian, Lithuanian) were closed down leaving only two media of instructions in the schools: Latvian and Russian.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       An influx of labourers, administrators, military personnel and their dependants from Russia and other Soviet republics started. By 1959 about 400,000 people arrived from other Soviet republics and the ethnic Latvian population had fallen to 62%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Since Latvia had maintained a well-developed infrastructure and educated specialists, Moscow decided to base some of the Soviet Union's most advanced manufacturing in Latvia. New industry was created in Latvia, including a major
       <a href="/wiki/Riga_Autobus_Factory" title="Riga Autobus Factory">
        machinery factory RAF
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Jelgava" title="Jelgava">
        Jelgava
       </a>
       , electrotechnical factories in
       <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">
        Riga
       </a>
       , chemical factories in
       <a href="/wiki/Daugavpils" title="Daugavpils">
        Daugavpils
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Valmiera" title="Valmiera">
        Valmiera
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Olaine" title="Olaine">
        Olaine
       </a>
       —and some food and oil processing plants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Latvia manufactured trains, ships, minibuses, mopeds, telephones, radios and hi-fi systems, electrical and diesel engines, textiles, furniture, clothing, bags and luggage, shoes, musical instruments, home appliances, watches, tools and equipment, aviation and agricultural equipment and long list of other goods. Latvia had its own film industry and musical records factory (LPs). However, there were not enough people to operate the newly built factories.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       To maintain and expand industrial production, skilled workers were migrating from all over the Soviet Union, decreasing the proportion of ethnic Latvians in the republic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Population of Latvia reached its peak in 1990 at just under 2.7 million people.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Restoration_of_Independence_in_1991">
        Restoration of Independence in 1991
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Restoration of Independence in 1991">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Singing_Revolution" title="Singing Revolution">
        Singing Revolution
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Way" title="Baltic Way">
        Baltic Way
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/On_the_Restoration_of_Independence_of_the_Republic_of_Latvia" title="On the Restoration of Independence of the Republic of Latvia">
        On the Restoration of Independence of the Republic of Latvia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the second half of the 1980s, Soviet leader
       <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">
        Mikhail Gorbachev
       </a>
       started to introduce political and economic reforms in the Soviet Union that were called
       <a href="/wiki/Glasnost" title="Glasnost">
        glasnost
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">
        perestroika
       </a>
       . In the summer of 1987, the first large demonstrations were held in Riga at the
       <a href="/wiki/Freedom_Monument" title="Freedom Monument">
        Freedom Monument
       </a>
       —a symbol of independence. In the summer of 1988, a national movement, coalescing in the
       <a href="/wiki/Popular_Front_of_Latvia" title="Popular Front of Latvia">
        Popular Front of Latvia
       </a>
       , was opposed by the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Front_of_the_Working_People_of_Latvia" title="International Front of the Working People of Latvia">
        Interfront
       </a>
       . The Latvian SSR, along with the other
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">
        Baltic Republics
       </a>
       was allowed greater autonomy, and in 1988, the old pre-war
       <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Latvia" title="Flag of Latvia">
        Flag of Latvia
       </a>
       flew again, replacing the Soviet Latvian flag as the official flag in 1990.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1989, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supreme_Soviet_of_the_USSR" title="Supreme Soviet of the USSR">
        Supreme Soviet of the USSR
       </a>
       adopted a resolution on the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Baltic_states" title="Occupation of the Baltic states">
         Occupation of the Baltic states
        </a>
       </i>
       , in which it declared the occupation "not in accordance with law", and not the "will of the Soviet people". Pro-independence Popular Front of Latvia candidates gained a two-thirds majority in the
       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Council_of_the_Republic_of_Latvia" title="Supreme Council of the Republic of Latvia">
        Supreme Council
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Supreme_Soviet_election,_1990" title="Latvian Supreme Soviet election, 1990">
        March 1990 democratic elections
       </a>
       . On 4 May 1990, the Supreme Council adopted the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Declaration_on_the_Restoration_of_Independence_of_the_Republic_of_Latvia" title="Declaration on the Restoration of Independence of the Republic of Latvia">
        Declaration on the Restoration of Independence of the Republic of Latvia
       </a>
       , and the Latvian SSR was renamed Republic of Latvia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Imagining_66-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Imagining-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       However, the central power in Moscow continued to regard Latvia as a Soviet republic in 1990 and 1991. In January 1991, Soviet political and military forces tried unsuccessfully to overthrow the Republic of Latvia authorities by occupying the central publishing house in Riga and establishing a Committee of National Salvation to usurp governmental functions. During the transitional period, Moscow maintained many central Soviet state authorities in Latvia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Imagining_66-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Imagining-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In spite of this, 73% of all Latvian residents confirmed their strong support for independence on 3 March 1991, in a nonbinding advisory referendum.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The Popular Front of Latvia advocated that all permanent residents be eligible for Latvian citizenship, and that helped sway a large number of ethnic Russians to vote for independence. However, universal citizenship for all permanent residents was not adopted. Instead, citizenship was granted to persons who had been citizens of Latvia at the day of loss of independence at 1940 as well as their descendants. As a consequence, the majority of ethnic non-Latvians did not receive Latvian citizenship since neither they nor their parents had ever been citizens of Latvia, becoming
       <a href="/wiki/Non-citizens_(Latvia)" title="Non-citizens (Latvia)">
        non-citizens
       </a>
       or citizens of other former Soviet republics. By 2011, more than half of non-citizens had taken naturalisation exams and received Latvian citizenship. Still, today there are 290,660 non-citizens in Latvia, which represent 14.1% of population. They have
       <a href="/wiki/Statelessness" title="Statelessness">
        no citizenship of any country
       </a>
       , and cannot vote in Latvia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Republic of Latvia declared the end of the transitional period and restored full independence on 21 August 1991, in the aftermath of the failed
       <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1991 Soviet coup d'état attempt">
        Soviet coup attempt
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FINemb_3-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FINemb-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="310" data-file-width="521" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/220px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/330px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/440px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Latvia became a member of the European Union in 2004 and signed the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lisbon_Treaty" title="Lisbon Treaty">
          Lisbon Treaty
         </a>
         in 2007.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Saeima" title="Saeima">
        Saeima
       </a>
       , Latvia's parliament, was again elected in 1993. Russia ended its military presence by completing its troop withdrawal in 1994 and shutting down the
       <a href="/wiki/Skrunda-1" title="Skrunda-1">
        Skrunda-1
       </a>
       radar station in 1998. The major goals of Latvia in the 1990s, to join
       <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">
        NATO
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       , were achieved in 2004. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NATO_Summit_2006" title="NATO Summit 2006">
        NATO Summit 2006
       </a>
       was held in Riga.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Language and citizenship laws have been opposed by many
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russophone" title="Russophone">
        Russophones
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Citizenship" title="Citizenship">
        Citizenship
       </a>
       was not automatically extended to former Soviet citizens who settled during the Soviet occupation, or to their offspring. Children born to non-nationals after the reestablishment of independence are automatically entitled to citizenship. Approximately 72% of Latvian citizens are Latvian, while 20% are Russian; less than 1% of non-citizens are Latvian, while 71% are Russian.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The government denationalised private property confiscated by the Soviets, returning it or compensating the owners for it, and
       <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">
        privatised
       </a>
       most state-owned industries, reintroducing the
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_lats" title="Latvian lats">
        prewar currency
       </a>
       . Albeit having experienced a difficult transition to a liberal economy and its re-orientation toward Western Europe, Latvia is one of the fastest growing economies in the European Union. In 2014,
       <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">
        Riga
       </a>
       was the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">
        European Capital of Culture
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">
        euro
       </a>
       was introduced as the currency of the country and a Latvian was named vice-president of the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">
        European Commission
       </a>
       . In 2015 Latvia held the presidency of
       <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">
        Council of the European Union
       </a>
       . Big European events have been celebrated in
       <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">
        Riga
       </a>
       such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest_2003" title="Eurovision Song Contest 2003">
        Eurovision Song Contest 2003
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/27th_European_Film_Awards" title="27th European Film Awards">
        European Film Awards 2014
       </a>
       . On 1 July 2016, Latvia became a member of the OECD.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Latvia" title="Geography of Latvia">
        Geography of Latvia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">
        Baltic Sea
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">
        Baltic states
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Europe" title="Northern Europe">
        Northern Europe
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Baltijos_j%C5%ABra_Kolkos_rage.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Baltijos_j%C5%ABra_Kolkos_rage.JPG/220px-Baltijos_j%C5%ABra_Kolkos_rage.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Baltijos_j%C5%ABra_Kolkos_rage.JPG/330px-Baltijos_j%C5%ABra_Kolkos_rage.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Baltijos_j%C5%ABra_Kolkos_rage.JPG/440px-Baltijos_j%C5%ABra_Kolkos_rage.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Baltijos_j%C5%ABra_Kolkos_rage.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Cape Kolka, the northern tip of Latvia in the Gulf of Riga
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BalticSea_March2000_NASA-S2000084115409_md.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="433" height="305" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/BalticSea_March2000_NASA-S2000084115409_md.jpg/220px-BalticSea_March2000_NASA-S2000084115409_md.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/BalticSea_March2000_NASA-S2000084115409_md.jpg/330px-BalticSea_March2000_NASA-S2000084115409_md.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/eb/BalticSea_March2000_NASA-S2000084115409_md.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BalticSea_March2000_NASA-S2000084115409_md.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Latvia lies in Northern Europe, on the eastern shores of the
         <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">
          Baltic Sea
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Latvia lies in Northern Europe, on the eastern shores of the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">
        Baltic Sea
       </a>
       and northwestern part of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_European_craton" title="East European craton">
        East European craton
       </a>
       , between latitudes
       <a href="/wiki/55th_parallel_north" title="55th parallel north">
        55°
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/58th_parallel_north" title="58th parallel north">
        58° N
       </a>
       (a small area is north of 58°), and longitudes
       <a href="/wiki/21st_meridian_east" title="21st meridian east">
        21°
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/29th_meridian_east" title="29th meridian east">
        29° E
       </a>
       (a small area is west of 21°). Latvia has a total area of 64,559 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (24,926 sq mi) of which 62,157 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (23,999 sq mi) land, 18,159 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (7,011 sq mi) agricultural land,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Agriculture_-_Key_Indicators_71-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Agriculture_-_Key_Indicators-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       34,964 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (13,500 sq mi) forest land
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forestry_-_Key_Indicators_72-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Forestry_-_Key_Indicators-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and 2,402 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (927 sq mi) inland water.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geographical_Data_-_Key_Indicators_73-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Geographical_Data_-_Key_Indicators-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The total length of Latvia's boundary is 1,866 km (1,159 mi). The total length of its land boundary is 1,368 km (850 mi), of which 343 km (213 mi) is shared with
       <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">
        Estonia
       </a>
       to the north, 276 km (171 mi) with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" title="Russian Federation">
        Russian Federation
       </a>
       to the east, 161 km (100 mi) with
       <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">
        Belarus
       </a>
       to the southeast and 588 km (365 mi) with
       <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">
        Lithuania
       </a>
       to the south. The total length of its
       <a href="/wiki/Maritime_boundary" title="Maritime boundary">
        maritime boundary
       </a>
       is 498 km (309 mi), which is shared with Estonia,
       <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">
        Sweden
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">
        Lithuania
       </a>
       . Extension from north to south is 210 km (130 mi) and from west to east 450 km (280 mi).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geographical_Data_-_Key_Indicators_73-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Geographical_Data_-_Key_Indicators-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Most of Latvia's territory is less than 100 m (330 ft)
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">
        above sea level
       </a>
       . Its largest lake,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lub%C4%81ns" title="Lubāns">
        Lubāns
       </a>
       , has an area of 80.7 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (31.2 sq mi), its deepest lake,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dr%C4%ABdzis" title="Drīdzis">
        Drīdzis
       </a>
       , is 65.1 m (214 ft) deep. The longest river on Latvian territory is the
       <a href="/wiki/Gauja" title="Gauja">
        Gauja
       </a>
       , at 452 km (281 mi) in length. The longest river flowing through Latvian territory is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daugava_River" title="Daugava River">
        Daugava
       </a>
       , which has a total length of 1,005 km (624 mi), of which 352 km (219 mi) is on Latvian territory. Latvia's highest point is
       <a href="/wiki/Gaizi%C5%86kalns" title="Gaiziņkalns">
        Gaiziņkalns
       </a>
       , 311.6 m (1,022 ft). The length of Latvia's
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">
        Baltic
       </a>
       coastline is 494 km (307 mi). An inlet of the Baltic Sea, the shallow
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Riga" title="Gulf of Riga">
        Gulf of Riga
       </a>
       is situated in the northwest of the country.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Latvia_in_brief_74-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Latvia_in_brief-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px">
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koppen_World_Map_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png">
           <img alt="Dfb" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="4231" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Koppen_World_Map_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png/200px-Koppen_World_Map_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Koppen_World_Map_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png/300px-Koppen_World_Map_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Koppen_World_Map_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png/400px-Koppen_World_Map_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png 2x" width="200"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
           <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #38C7FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
           </span>
           Humid continental climate warm summer subtype
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koppen_classification_worldmap_CfbCfc.png">
           <img alt="Cfb" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="2000" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Koppen_classification_worldmap_CfbCfc.png/200px-Koppen_classification_worldmap_CfbCfc.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Koppen_classification_worldmap_CfbCfc.png/300px-Koppen_classification_worldmap_CfbCfc.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Koppen_classification_worldmap_CfbCfc.png/400px-Koppen_classification_worldmap_CfbCfc.png 2x" width="200"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
           <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #008000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
           </span>
           Oceanic climate
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div style="clear:left">
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Latvia has a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperate" title="Temperate">
        temperate
       </a>
       climate that has been described in various sources as either
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humid_continental" title="Humid continental">
        humid continental
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate#Dfb/Dwb/Dsb:_Warm_summer_subtype" title="Humid continental climate">
        Köppen
        <i>
         Dfb
        </i>
       </a>
       ) or
       <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">
        oceanic/maritime
       </a>
       (Köppen
       <i>
        Cfb
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liepu_75-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-liepu-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Coastal regions, especially the western coast of
       <a href="/wiki/Courland_Peninsula" title="Courland Peninsula">
        Courland Peninsula
       </a>
       , possess a more maritime climate with cooler summers and milder winters, while eastern parts exhibit a more continental climate with warmer summers and harsher winters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liepu_75-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-liepu-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Latvia has four pronounced seasons of near-equal length. Winter starts in mid-December and lasts until mid-March. Winters have average temperatures of −6 °C (21 °F) and are characterized by stable snow cover, bright sunshine, and short days. Severe spells of winter weather with cold winds, extreme temperatures of around −30 °C (−22 °F) and heavy snowfalls are common. Summer starts in June and lasts until August. Summers are usually warm and sunny, with cool evenings and nights. Summers have average temperatures of around 19 °C (66 °F), with extremes of 35 °C (95 °F). Spring and autumn bring fairly mild weather.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">
        Environment
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Environment">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Turaidas_skats_uz_Gauju_2okt04.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Turaidas_skats_uz_Gauju_2okt04.JPG/220px-Turaidas_skats_uz_Gauju_2okt04.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Turaidas_skats_uz_Gauju_2okt04.JPG/330px-Turaidas_skats_uz_Gauju_2okt04.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Turaidas_skats_uz_Gauju_2okt04.JPG/440px-Turaidas_skats_uz_Gauju_2okt04.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Turaidas_skats_uz_Gauju_2okt04.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Latvia has the fifth highest proportion of land covered by forests in the European Union.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Most of the country is composed of fertile lowland plains and moderate hills. In a typical Latvian landscape, a mosaic of vast forests alternates with fields, farmsteads, and pastures. Arable land is spotted with birch groves and wooded clusters, which afford a habitat for numerous plants and animals. Latvia has hundreds of kilometres of undeveloped seashore—lined by pine forests, dunes, and continuous white sand beaches.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Latvia_in_brief_74-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Latvia_in_brief-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia_80-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Latvia has the 5th highest proportion of land covered by forests in the European Union, after Sweden, Finland, Estonia and Slovenia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Forests account for 3,497,000 ha (8,640,000 acres) or 56% of the total land area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forestry_-_Key_Indicators_72-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Forestry_-_Key_Indicators-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Latvia has over 12,500 rivers, which stretch for 38,000 km (24,000 mi). Major rivers include the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daugava_River" title="Daugava River">
        Daugava River
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lielupe" title="Lielupe">
        Lielupe
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gauja" title="Gauja">
        Gauja
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Venta" title="Venta">
        Venta
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Salaca" title="Salaca">
        Salaca
       </a>
       , the largest spawning ground for
       <a href="/wiki/Salmon" title="Salmon">
        salmon
       </a>
       in the eastern Baltics. There are 2,256 lakes that are bigger than 1 ha (2.5 acres), with a collective area of 1,000 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (390 sq mi).
       <a href="/wiki/Mire" title="Mire">
        Mires
       </a>
       occupy 9.9% of Latvia's territory. Of these, 42% are raised bogs; 49% are fens; and 9% are transitional mires. 70% percent of the mires are untouched by civilisation, and they are a refuge for many rare species of plants and animals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia_80-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Agricultural areas account for 1,815,900 ha (4,487,000 acres) or 29% of the total land area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Agriculture_-_Key_Indicators_71-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Agriculture_-_Key_Indicators-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       With the dismantling of collective farms, the area devoted to farming decreased dramatically – now farms are predominantly small. Approximately 200 farms, occupying 2,750 ha (6,800 acres), are engaged in ecologically pure farming (using no artificial fertilisers or pesticides).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia_80-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Latvia's
       <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">
        national parks
       </a>
       are
       <a href="/wiki/Gauja_National_Park" title="Gauja National Park">
        Gauja National Park
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Vidzeme" title="Vidzeme">
        Vidzeme
       </a>
       (since 1973)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/%C4%B6emeri_National_Park" title="Ķemeri National Park">
        Ķemeri National Park
       </a>
       in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zemgale" title="Zemgale">
        Zemgale
       </a>
       (1997),
       <a href="/wiki/Sl%C4%ABtere_National_Park" title="Slītere National Park">
        Slītere National Park
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Courland" title="Courland">
        Kurzeme
       </a>
       (1999), and
       <a href="/wiki/R%C4%81zna_National_Park" title="Rāzna National Park">
        Rāzna National Park
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Latgale" title="Latgale">
        Latgale
       </a>
       (2007).
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Latvia has a long tradition of conservation. The first laws and regulations were promulgated in the 16th and 17th centuries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia_80-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are 706 specially state-level protected natural areas in Latvia: four national parks, one biosphere reserve, 42 nature parks, nine areas of protected landscapes, 260 nature reserves, four strict nature reserves, 355 nature monuments, seven protected marine areas and 24 microreserves.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nationally protected areas account for 12,790 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (4,940 sq mi) or around 20% of Latvia's total land area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geographical_Data_-_Key_Indicators_73-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Geographical_Data_-_Key_Indicators-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Latvia's Red Book (Endangered Species List of Latvia), which was established in 1977, contains 112 plant species and 119 animal species. Latvia has ratified the international Washington, Bern, and Ramsare conventions.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia_80-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The 2012
       <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index" title="Environmental Performance Index">
        Environmental Performance Index
       </a>
       ranks Latvia second, after
       <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">
        Switzerland
       </a>
       , based on the environmental performance of the country's policies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">
        <div style="width: 162px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;">

          </p>

           <a href="/wiki/Devonian" title="Devonian">

           </a>
           sandstone cliffs in
           <a href="/wiki/Gauja_National_Park" title="Gauja National Park">
            Gauja National Park
           </a>
           , Latvia's largest and oldest national park
          </p>
         </div>

       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">

           </a>

          <p>
           <a href="/wiki/%C4%B6emeri_National_Park" title="Ķemeri National Park">
            Ķemeri National Park
           </a>
           is home to mires, natural mineral-springs, muds and lakes that are former lagoons of the
           <a href="/wiki/Littorina_Sea" title="Littorina Sea">
            Littorina Sea
           </a>
           .
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>

           </a>

            Livonian
           </a>
           fishing villages of the
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Livonian_Coast" title="Livonian Coast">
            Livonian Coast
           </a>
           . (
           <a href="/wiki/Livonian_language" title="Livonian language">
            Livonian
           </a>
           :
           <i>
            Līvõd Rānda
           </i>
           )
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">
        Biodiversity
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:White-Wagtail.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="571" data-file-width="732" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/White-Wagtail.jpg/220px-White-Wagtail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/White-Wagtail.jpg/330px-White-Wagtail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/White-Wagtail.jpg/440px-White-Wagtail.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:White-Wagtail.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/White_wagtail" title="White wagtail">
          white wagtail
         </a>
         is the national bird of Latvia.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
          <a href="#cite_note-85">
           [85]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Approximately 30,000 species of flora and fauna have been registered in Latvia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Common species of wildlife in Latvia include
       <a href="/wiki/Roe_deer" title="Roe deer">
        deer
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">
        wild boar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Moose" title="Moose">
        moose
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_lynx" title="Eurasian lynx">
        lynx
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Brown_bear" title="Brown bear">
        bear
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Red_fox" title="Red fox">
        fox
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_beaver" title="Eurasian beaver">
        beaver
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Gray_wolf" title="Gray wolf">
        wolves
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_non-marine_molluscs_of_Latvia" title="List of non-marine molluscs of Latvia">
        Non-marine molluscs of Latvia
       </a>
       include 159 species.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Species that are endangered in other European countries but common in Latvia include: black stork (
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ciconia_nigra" title="Ciconia nigra">
         Ciconia nigra
        </a>
       </i>
       ), corncrake (
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crex_crex" title="Crex crex">
         Crex crex
        </a>
       </i>
       ), lesser spotted eagle (
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aquila_pomarina" title="Aquila pomarina">
         Aquila pomarina
        </a>
       </i>
       ), white-backed woodpecker (
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Picoides_leucotos" title="Picoides leucotos">
         Picoides leucotos
        </a>
       </i>
       ), Eurasian crane (
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grus_grus" title="Grus grus">
         Grus grus
        </a>
       </i>
       ), Eurasian beaver (
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castor_fiber" title="Castor fiber">
         Castor fiber
        </a>
       </i>
       ), Eurasian otter (
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutra_lutra" title="Lutra lutra">
         Lutra lutra
        </a>
       </i>
       ), European wolf (
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canis_lupus" title="Canis lupus">
         Canis lupus
        </a>
       </i>
       ) and European lynx (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_lynx" title="Eurasian lynx">
         Felis lynx
        </a>
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia_80-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">
        Phytogeographically
       </a>
       , Latvia is shared between the Central European and Northern European provinces of the
       <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">
        Circumboreal Region
       </a>
       within the
       <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">
        Boreal Kingdom
       </a>
       . According to the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">
        WWF
       </a>
       , the territory of Latvia belongs to the
       <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">
        ecoregion
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Sarmatic_mixed_forests" title="Sarmatic mixed forests">
        Sarmatic mixed forests
       </a>
       . 56 percent
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Forestry_-_Key_Indicators_72-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Forestry_-_Key_Indicators-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       of Latvia's territory is covered by forests, mostly
       <a href="/wiki/Scots_pine" title="Scots pine">
        Scots pine
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Birch" title="Birch">
        birch
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norway_spruce" title="Norway spruce">
        Norway spruce
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Several species of flora and fauna are considered national symbols.
       <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">
        Oak
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Quercus_robur" title="Quercus robur">
         Quercus robur
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">
        Latvian
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="lv">
         ozols
        </span>
       </i>
       ), and
       <a href="/wiki/Tilia" title="Tilia">
        linden
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Tilia_cordata" title="Tilia cordata">
         Tilia cordata
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">
        Latvian
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="lv">
         liepa
        </span>
       </i>
       ) are Latvia's national trees and the
       <a href="/wiki/Leucanthemum_vulgare" title="Leucanthemum vulgare">
        daisy
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Leucanthemum_vulgare" title="Leucanthemum vulgare">
         Leucanthemum vulgare
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">
        Latvian
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="lv">
         pīpene
        </span>
       </i>
       ) its national flower. The white wagtail (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/White_wagtail" title="White wagtail">
         Motacilla alba
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">
        Latvian
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="lv">
         baltā cielava
        </span>
       </i>
       ) is Latvia's national bird. Its national insect is the
       <a href="/wiki/Adalia_bipunctata" title="Adalia bipunctata">
        two-spot ladybird
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Adalia_bipunctata" title="Adalia bipunctata">
         Adalia bipunctata
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">
        Latvian
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="lv">
         divpunktu mārīte
        </span>
       </i>
       ).
       <a href="/wiki/Amber" title="Amber">
        Amber
       </a>
       , fossilized tree resin, is one of Latvia's most important cultural symbols. In ancient times, amber found along the Baltic Sea coast was sought by Vikings as well as traders from Egypt, Greece and the Roman Empire. This led to the development of the
       <a href="/wiki/Amber_Road" title="Amber Road">
        Amber Road
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Several nature reserves protect unspoiled landscapes with a variety of large animals. At
       <a href="/wiki/Pape_Nature_Reserve" title="Pape Nature Reserve">
        Pape Nature Reserve
       </a>
       , where
       <a href="/wiki/European_bison" title="European bison">
        European bison
       </a>
       , wild horses, and
       <a href="/wiki/Heck_cattle" title="Heck cattle">
        recreated aurochs
       </a>
       have been reintroduced, there is now an almost complete
       <a href="/wiki/Holocene" title="Holocene">
        Holocene
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Megafauna" title="Megafauna">
        megafauna
       </a>
       also including moose, deer, and wolf.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">
        Administrative divisions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:362px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Latvija_viki.PNG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="620" data-file-width="1001" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Latvija_viki.PNG/360px-Latvija_viki.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Latvija_viki.PNG/540px-Latvija_viki.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Latvija_viki.PNG/720px-Latvija_viki.PNG 2x" width="360"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Latvija_viki.PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Historical regions: orange
         <a href="/wiki/Courland" title="Courland">
          Courland
         </a>
         , green
         <a href="/wiki/Semigallia" title="Semigallia">
          Semigallia
         </a>
         , brown
         <a href="/wiki/Selonia" title="Selonia">
          Selonia
         </a>
         , yellow
         <a href="/wiki/Vidzeme" title="Vidzeme">
          Vidzeme
         </a>
         , blue
         <a href="/wiki/Latgale" title="Latgale">
          Latgale
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:362px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Latvijas_novadi_(kr%C4%81s%C4%81s).png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2536" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Latvijas_novadi_%28kr%C4%81s%C4%81s%29.png/360px-Latvijas_novadi_%28kr%C4%81s%C4%81s%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Latvijas_novadi_%28kr%C4%81s%C4%81s%29.png/540px-Latvijas_novadi_%28kr%C4%81s%C4%81s%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Latvijas_novadi_%28kr%C4%81s%C4%81s%29.png/720px-Latvijas_novadi_%28kr%C4%81s%C4%81s%29.png 2x" width="360"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Latvijas_novadi_(kr%C4%81s%C4%81s).png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Administrative divisions of Latvia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Latvia" title="Administrative divisions of Latvia">
        Administrative divisions of Latvia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Latvia" title="List of cities in Latvia">
        List of cities in Latvia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Planning_regions_of_Latvia" title="Planning regions of Latvia">
        Planning regions of Latvia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Statistical_regions_of_Latvia" title="Statistical regions of Latvia">
        Statistical regions of Latvia
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historical_regions_of_Latvia" title="Historical regions of Latvia">
        Historical regions of Latvia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Latvia is a
       <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">
        unitary state
       </a>
       , currently divided into 110 one-level municipalities (
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">
        Latvian
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="lv">
         novadi
        </span>
       </i>
       ) and 9 republican cities (
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">
        Latvian
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="lv">
         republikas pilsētas
        </span>
       </i>
       ) with their own city council and administration:
       <a href="/wiki/Daugavpils" title="Daugavpils">
        Daugavpils
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/J%C4%93kabpils" title="Jēkabpils">
        Jēkabpils
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jelgava" title="Jelgava">
        Jelgava
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/J%C5%ABrmala" title="Jūrmala">
        Jūrmala
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Liep%C4%81ja" title="Liepāja">
        Liepāja
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/R%C4%93zekne" title="Rēzekne">
        Rēzekne
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">
        Riga
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Valmiera" title="Valmiera">
        Valmiera
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Ventspils" title="Ventspils">
        Ventspils
       </a>
       . There are four
       <a href="/wiki/Cultural_regions_of_Latvia" title="Cultural regions of Latvia">
        historical and cultural regions in Latvia
       </a>
       –
       <a href="/wiki/Courland" title="Courland">
        Courland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latgale" title="Latgale">
        Latgale
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Vidzeme" title="Vidzeme">
        Vidzeme
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zemgale" title="Zemgale">
        Zemgale
       </a>
       , which are recognised in
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Latvia" title="Constitution of Latvia">
        Constitution of Latvia
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Selonia" title="Selonia">
        Selonia
       </a>
       , a part of Zemgale, is sometimes considered culturally distinct region, but it is not part of any formal division. The borders of historical and cultural regions usually are not explicitly defined and in several sources may vary. In formal divisions, Riga region, which includes the capital and parts of other regions that have a strong relationship with the capital, is also often included in regional divisions; e.g., there are five
       <a href="/wiki/Planning_regions_of_Latvia" title="Planning regions of Latvia">
        planning regions of Latvia
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">
        Latvian
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="lv">
         plānošanas reģioni
        </span>
       </i>
       ), which were created in 2009 to promote balanced development of all regions. Under this division Riga region includes large parts of what traditionally is considered Vidzeme, Courland, and Zemgale.
       <a href="/wiki/Statistical_regions_of_Latvia" title="Statistical regions of Latvia">
        Statistical regions of Latvia
       </a>
       , established in accordance with the EU
       <a href="/wiki/Nomenclature_of_Territorial_Units_for_Statistics" title="Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics">
        Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics
       </a>
       , duplicate this division, but divides Riga region into two parts with the capital alone being a separate region.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The largest city in Latvia is Riga, the second largest city is Daugavpils and the third largest city is Liepaja.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">
        Politics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Politics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Latvia" title="Politics of Latvia">
        Politics of Latvia
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Latvia" title="Parliament of Latvia">
        Parliament of Latvia
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Latvia" title="Government of Latvia">
        Government of Latvia
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:left; float:left; margin-right:9px; margin-left:2px;">
       <tr>
        <td style="text-align:left;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Saeima_-_10.Saeimas_deput%C4%81ts_Raimonds_V%C4%93jonis.jpg">
