         </a>
        </td>
        <td style="text-align:left;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Saeima_-_10.Saeimas_deput%C4%81ts_M%C4%81ris_Ku%C4%8Dinskis.jpg">
          <img alt="Flickr - Saeima - 10.Saeimas deputāts Māris Kučinskis.jpg" data-file-height="1504" data-file-width="1000" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Flickr_-_Saeima_-_10.Saeimas_deput%C4%81ts_M%C4%81ris_Ku%C4%8Dinskis.jpg/125px-Flickr_-_Saeima_-_10.Saeimas_deput%C4%81ts_M%C4%81ris_Ku%C4%8Dinskis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Flickr_-_Saeima_-_10.Saeimas_deput%C4%81ts_M%C4%81ris_Ku%C4%8Dinskis.jpg/188px-Flickr_-_Saeima_-_10.Saeimas_deput%C4%81ts_M%C4%81ris_Ku%C4%8Dinskis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Flickr_-_Saeima_-_10.Saeimas_deput%C4%81ts_M%C4%81ris_Ku%C4%8Dinskis.jpg/250px-Flickr_-_Saeima_-_10.Saeimas_deput%C4%81ts_M%C4%81ris_Ku%C4%8Dinskis.jpg 2x" width="125"/>
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="text-align:center;">
         <a href="/wiki/Raimonds_V%C4%93jonis" title="Raimonds Vējonis">
          Raimonds Vējonis
         </a>
         <br/>
         <small>
          <a href="/wiki/President_of_Latvia" title="President of Latvia">
           President
          </a>
         </small>
        </td>
        <td style="text-align:center;">
         <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ris_Ku%C4%8Dinskis" title="Māris Kučinskis">
          Māris Kučinskis
         </a>
         <br/>
         <small>
          <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Latvia" title="Prime Minister of Latvia">
           Prime Minister
          </a>
         </small>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The 100-seat
       <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">
        unicameral
       </a>
       Latvian parliament, the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Saeima" title="Saeima">
         Saeima
        </a>
       </i>
       , is
       <a href="/wiki/General_election" title="General election">
        elected
       </a>
       by direct popular vote every four years. The president is elected by the
       <i>
        Saeima
       </i>
       in a separate election, also held every four years. The president appoints a prime minister who, together with his cabinet, forms the
       <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">
        executive branch
       </a>
       of the government, which has to receive a confidence vote by the
       <i>
        Saeima
       </i>
       . This system also existed before
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Constitution_90-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Constitution-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The most senior civil servants are the thirteen
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State" title="Secretary of State">
        Secretaries of State
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Saeima_-_4.maijs_Saeim%C4%81_(6).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Flickr_-_Saeima_-_4.maijs_Saeim%C4%81_%286%29.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_Saeima_-_4.maijs_Saeim%C4%81_%286%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Flickr_-_Saeima_-_4.maijs_Saeim%C4%81_%286%29.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_Saeima_-_4.maijs_Saeim%C4%81_%286%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Flickr_-_Saeima_-_4.maijs_Saeim%C4%81_%286%29.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_Saeima_-_4.maijs_Saeim%C4%81_%286%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Saeima_-_4.maijs_Saeim%C4%81_(6).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/House_of_the_Livonian_Noble_Corporation" title="House of the Livonian Noble Corporation">
          building
         </a>
         of the
         <i>
          Saeima
         </i>
         , the parliament of Latvia, in Riga
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">
        Foreign relations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Latvia" title="Foreign relations of Latvia">
        Foreign relations of Latvia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ministerio_de_Asuntos_Exteriores,_Riga,_Letonia,_2012-08-07,_DD_01.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2563" data-file-width="4021" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Ministerio_de_Asuntos_Exteriores%2C_Riga%2C_Letonia%2C_2012-08-07%2C_DD_01.JPG/220px-Ministerio_de_Asuntos_Exteriores%2C_Riga%2C_Letonia%2C_2012-08-07%2C_DD_01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Ministerio_de_Asuntos_Exteriores%2C_Riga%2C_Letonia%2C_2012-08-07%2C_DD_01.JPG/330px-Ministerio_de_Asuntos_Exteriores%2C_Riga%2C_Letonia%2C_2012-08-07%2C_DD_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Ministerio_de_Asuntos_Exteriores%2C_Riga%2C_Letonia%2C_2012-08-07%2C_DD_01.JPG/440px-Ministerio_de_Asuntos_Exteriores%2C_Riga%2C_Letonia%2C_2012-08-07%2C_DD_01.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ministerio_de_Asuntos_Exteriores,_Riga,_Letonia,_2012-08-07,_DD_01.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The building of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Riga
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Latvia is a member of the United Nations,
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">
        Council of Europe
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">
        NATO
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">
        OECD
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">
        OSCE
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">
        IMF
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">
        WTO
       </a>
       . It is also a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Baltic_Sea_States" title="Council of the Baltic Sea States">
        Council of the Baltic Sea States
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Investment_Bank" title="Nordic Investment Bank">
        Nordic Investment Bank
       </a>
       . It was a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">
        League of Nations
       </a>
       (1921–1946). Latvia is part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">
        Schengen Area
       </a>
       and joined the
       <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">
        Eurozone
       </a>
       on 1 January 2014.
      </p>
      <p>
       Latvia has established diplomatic relations with 158 countries. It has 44 diplomatic and consular missions and maintains 34 embassies and 9 permanent representations abroad. There are 37 foreign embassies and 11 international organisations in Latvia's capital
       <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">
        Riga
       </a>
       . Latvia hosts one European Union institution, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Body_of_European_Regulators_of_Electronic_Communications" title="Body of European Regulators of Electronic Communications">
        Body of European Regulators for Electronic Communications
       </a>
       (BEREC).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Latvia's foreign policy priorities include co-operation in the Baltic Sea region, European integration, active involvement in international organisations, contribution to European and transatlantic security and defence structures, participation in international civilian and military peacekeeping operations, and development co-operation, particularly the strengthening of stability and democracy in the EU's
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Partnership" title="Eastern Partnership">
        Eastern Partnership
       </a>
       countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Foreign_Ministers_of_Nordic_and_Baltic_countries_met_in_Helsinki,_30.08.2011_(Photographer_Eero_Kuosmanen).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="5616" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Foreign_Ministers_of_Nordic_and_Baltic_countries_met_in_Helsinki%2C_30.08.2011_%28Photographer_Eero_Kuosmanen%29.jpg/220px-Foreign_Ministers_of_Nordic_and_Baltic_countries_met_in_Helsinki%2C_30.08.2011_%28Photographer_Eero_Kuosmanen%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Foreign_Ministers_of_Nordic_and_Baltic_countries_met_in_Helsinki%2C_30.08.2011_%28Photographer_Eero_Kuosmanen%29.jpg/330px-Foreign_Ministers_of_Nordic_and_Baltic_countries_met_in_Helsinki%2C_30.08.2011_%28Photographer_Eero_Kuosmanen%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Foreign_Ministers_of_Nordic_and_Baltic_countries_met_in_Helsinki%2C_30.08.2011_%28Photographer_Eero_Kuosmanen%29.jpg/440px-Foreign_Ministers_of_Nordic_and_Baltic_countries_met_in_Helsinki%2C_30.08.2011_%28Photographer_Eero_Kuosmanen%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Foreign_Ministers_of_Nordic_and_Baltic_countries_met_in_Helsinki,_30.08.2011_(Photographer_Eero_Kuosmanen).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Foreign ministers of the Nordic and Baltic countries in Helsinki, 2011
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Since the early 1990s, Latvia has been involved in active trilateral
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">
        Baltic states
       </a>
       co-operation with its neighbours
       <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">
        Estonia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">
        Lithuania
       </a>
       , and Nordic-Baltic co-operation with the
       <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">
        Nordic countries
       </a>
       . The Baltic Council is the joint forum of the interparliamentary
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Assembly" title="Baltic Assembly">
        Baltic Assembly
       </a>
       (BA) and the intergovernmental Baltic Council of Ministers (BCM).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NB8" title="NB8">
        Nordic-Baltic Eight
       </a>
       (NB-8) is the joint co-operation of the governments of Denmark, Estonia, Finland, Iceland, Latvia, Lithuania, Norway, and Sweden.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-http_97-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-http-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nordic-Baltic Six (NB-6), comprising Nordic-Baltic countries that are European Union member states, is a framework for meetings on EU-related issues. Interparliamentary co-operation between the Baltic Assembly and
       <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Council" title="Nordic Council">
        Nordic Council
       </a>
       was signed in 1992 and since 2006 annual meetings are held as well as regular meetings on other levels.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-http_97-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-http-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Joint Nordic-Baltic co-operation initiatives include the education programme NordPlus
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and mobility programmes for public administration,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       business and industry
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and culture.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nordic_Council_of_Ministers" title="Nordic Council of Ministers">
        Nordic Council of Ministers
       </a>
       has an office in Riga.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Latvia participates in the
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Dimension" title="Northern Dimension">
        Northern Dimension
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea_Region_Programme" title="Baltic Sea Region Programme">
        Baltic Sea Region Programme
       </a>
       , European Union initiatives to foster cross-border co-operation in the Baltic Sea region and Northern Europe. The secretariat of the Northern Dimension Partnership on Culture (NDPC) will be located in Riga.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2013 Riga hosted the annual
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Future_Forum" title="Northern Future Forum">
        Northern Future Forum
       </a>
       , a two-day informal meeting of the prime ministers of the Nordic-Baltic countries and the UK.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Enhanced Partnership in Northern Europe or
       <i>
        e-Pine
       </i>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">
        U.S. Department of State
       </a>
       diplomatic framework for co-operation with the Nordic-Baltic countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Latvia hosted the
       <a href="/wiki/2006_Riga_summit" title="2006 Riga summit">
        2006 NATO Summit
       </a>
       and since then the annual Riga Conference has become a leading foreign and security policy forum in Northern Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [106]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Latvia held the
       <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_the_Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Presidency of the Council of the European Union">
        Presidency of the Council of the European Union
       </a>
       in the first half of 2015.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">
        Human rights
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Human rights">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Latvia" title="Human rights in Latvia">
        Human rights in Latvia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pasport_negrazhdanina_Latvii_oblozhka.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="354" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Pasport_negrazhdanina_Latvii_oblozhka.JPG/150px-Pasport_negrazhdanina_Latvii_oblozhka.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Pasport_negrazhdanina_Latvii_oblozhka.JPG/225px-Pasport_negrazhdanina_Latvii_oblozhka.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Pasport_negrazhdanina_Latvii_oblozhka.JPG/300px-Pasport_negrazhdanina_Latvii_oblozhka.JPG 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pasport_negrazhdanina_Latvii_oblozhka.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Non-citizen passport
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to the reports by
       <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">
        Freedom House
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">
        US Department of State
       </a>
       , human rights in Latvia are generally respected by the government:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-departmentofstate1_107-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-departmentofstate1-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freedomhouse1_108-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse1-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Latvia is ranked above-average among the world's sovereign states in democracy,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-democracy1_109-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-democracy1-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Press_freedom" title="Press freedom">
        press freedom
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pressfree1_110-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-pressfree1-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Privacy" title="Privacy">
        privacy
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-privacy1_111-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-privacy1-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Human_development_(humanity)" title="Human development (humanity)">
        human development
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-human1_112-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-human1-112">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The country has a large
       <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_Latvia" title="Russians in Latvia">
        ethnic Russian
       </a>
       community, which was guaranteed basic rights under the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Latvia" title="Constitution of Latvia">
        constitution
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/International_human_rights_law" title="International human rights law">
        international human rights laws
       </a>
       ratified by the Latvian government.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-departmentofstate1_107-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-departmentofstate1-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freedomhouse2_113-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse2-113">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Approximately 270,000
       <a href="/wiki/Non-citizens_(Latvia)" title="Non-citizens (Latvia)">
        non-citizens
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
        <a href="#cite_note-114">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
       – including
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stateless_persons" title="Stateless persons">
        stateless persons
       </a>
       – have limited access to some political rights – only citizens are allowed to participate in parliamentary or municipal elections, although there are no limitations in regards to joining political parties or other political organizations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
        <a href="#cite_note-115">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
        <a href="#cite_note-116">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2011, the
       <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">
        OSCE
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/High_Commissioner_on_National_Minorities" title="High Commissioner on National Minorities">
        High Commissioner on National Minorities
       </a>
       "urged Latvia to allow non-citizens to vote in municipal elections."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Additionally, there have been reports of police abuse of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Detainee" title="Detainee">
        detainees
       </a>
       and arrestees, poor prison conditions and overcrowding, judicial corruption, discrimination against women, incidents of violence against
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_minorities" title="Ethnic minorities">
        ethnic minorities
       </a>
       , and societal violence and incidents of government discrimination against homosexuals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-departmentofstate1_107-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-departmentofstate1-107">
         [107]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-amnesty2009_118-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-amnesty2009-118">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-humarightswatch1_119-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-humarightswatch1-119">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2016,
       <a href="/wiki/Nils_U%C5%A1akovs" title="Nils Ušakovs">
        Nils Ušakovs
       </a>
       , the first ethnic Russian
       <a href="/wiki/Riga_City_Council" title="Riga City Council">
        mayor of Riga
       </a>
       in independent Latvia, has been fined by Latvia's
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_State_Language_Center" title="Latvian State Language Center">
        State Language Center
       </a>
       for posting in
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">
        Russian
       </a>
       on Facebook.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Military">
        Military
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Military">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Latvia" title="Military of Latvia">
        Military of Latvia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Naval_visit,_Belfast_(3)_-_geograph.org.uk_-_667223.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="414" data-file-width="640" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Naval_visit%2C_Belfast_%283%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_667223.jpg/220px-Naval_visit%2C_Belfast_%283%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_667223.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Naval_visit%2C_Belfast_%283%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_667223.jpg/330px-Naval_visit%2C_Belfast_%283%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_667223.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Naval_visit%2C_Belfast_%283%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_667223.jpg/440px-Naval_visit%2C_Belfast_%283%29_-_geograph.org.uk_-_667223.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Naval_visit,_Belfast_(3)_-_geograph.org.uk_-_667223.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Naval Forces minehunter
         <i>
          Imanta
         </i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:I%E2%80%99m_with_you_battle_buddy_141120-A-LY282-013.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1999" data-file-width="3631" height="121" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/I%E2%80%99m_with_you_battle_buddy_141120-A-LY282-013.jpg/220px-I%E2%80%99m_with_you_battle_buddy_141120-A-LY282-013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/I%E2%80%99m_with_you_battle_buddy_141120-A-LY282-013.jpg/330px-I%E2%80%99m_with_you_battle_buddy_141120-A-LY282-013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/I%E2%80%99m_with_you_battle_buddy_141120-A-LY282-013.jpg/440px-I%E2%80%99m_with_you_battle_buddy_141120-A-LY282-013.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:I%E2%80%99m_with_you_battle_buddy_141120-A-LY282-013.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Latvian soldiers during an exercise
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Latvia" title="Military of Latvia">
        National Armed Forces
       </a>
       (Latvian:
       <i>
        Nacionālie Bruņotie Spēki (NAF)
       </i>
       ) of Latvia consists of the
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Land_Forces" title="Latvian Land Forces">
        Land Forces
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Naval_Forces" title="Latvian Naval Forces">
        Naval Forces
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Air_Force" title="Latvian Air Force">
        Air Force
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_National_Guard" title="Latvian National Guard">
        National Guard
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Special_Tasks_Unit" title="Latvian Special Tasks Unit">
        Special Tasks Unit
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Military_Police" title="Latvian Military Police">
        Military Police
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_National_Armed_Forces_Staff_Battalion" title="Latvian National Armed Forces Staff Battalion">
        NAF staff Battalion
       </a>
       , Training and Doctrine Command, and Logistics Command. Latvia's defence concept is based upon the Swedish-Finnish model of a rapid response force composed of a mobilisation base and a small group of career professionals. From 1 January 2007, Latvia switched to a professional fully contract-based army.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         [121]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Latvia participates in international peacekeeping and security operations. Latvian armed forces have contributed to
       <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">
        NATO
       </a>
       and EU military operations in Bosnia and Herzegovina (1996–2009), Albania (1999), Kosovo (2000–2009), Macedonia (2003), Iraq (2005–2006), Afghanistan (since 2003), Somalia (since 2011) and Mali (since 2013).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_122-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-122">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Previous_operations_123-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Previous_operations-123">
         [123]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
        <a href="#cite_note-124">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Latvia also took part in the US-led
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multi-National_Force_-_Iraq" title="Multi-National Force - Iraq">
        Multi-National Force
       </a>
       operation in Iraq (2003–2008)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
        <a href="#cite_note-125">
         [125]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OSCE" title="OSCE">
        OSCE
       </a>
       missions in Georgia, Kosovo and Macedonia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
        <a href="#cite_note-126">
         [126]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Latvian armed forces contributed to a UK-led
       <a href="/wiki/EU_Battlegroup" title="EU Battlegroup">
        Battlegroup
       </a>
       in 2013 and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nordic_Battle_Group" title="Nordic Battle Group">
        Nordic Battlegroup
       </a>
       in 2015 under the
       <a href="/wiki/Common_Security_and_Defence_Policy" title="Common Security and Defence Policy">
        Common Security and Defence Policy
       </a>
       (CSDP) of the European Union.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
        <a href="#cite_note-127">
         [127]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Latvia acts as the lead nation in the coordination of the
       <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)#Northern_Distribution_Network" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">
        Northern Distribution Network
       </a>
       for transportation of non-lethal
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISAF" title="ISAF">
        ISAF
       </a>
       cargo by air and rail to Afghanistan.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
        <a href="#cite_note-128">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
        <a href="#cite_note-129">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
        <a href="#cite_note-130">
         [130]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is part of the Nordic Transition Support Unit (NTSU), which renders joint force contributions in support of Afghan security structures ahead of the withdrawal of Nordic and Baltic ISAF forces in 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
        <a href="#cite_note-131">
         [131]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since 1996 more than 3600 military personnel have participated in international operations,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Previous_operations_123-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Previous_operations-123">
         [123]
        </a>
       </sup>
       of whom 7 soldiers perished.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
        <a href="#cite_note-132">
         [132]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Per capita, Latvia is one of the largest contributors to international military operations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
        <a href="#cite_note-133">
         [133]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Latvian civilian experts have contributed to EU civilian missions: border assistance mission to Moldova and Ukraine (2005–2009), rule of law missions in Iraq (2006 and 2007) and Kosovo (since 2008), police mission in Afghanistan (since 2007) and monitoring mission in Georgia (since 2008).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_122-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-122">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Since March 2004, when the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">
        Baltic states
       </a>
       joined NATO, fighter jets of NATO members have been deployed on a rotational basis for the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Air_Policing" title="Baltic Air Policing">
        Baltic Air Policing
       </a>
       mission at
       <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0iauliai_International_Airport" title="Šiauliai International Airport">
        Šiauliai Airport
       </a>
       in Lithuania to guard the Baltic airspace. Latvia participates in several
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NATO_Centres_of_Excellence" title="NATO Centres of Excellence">
        NATO Centres of Excellence
       </a>
       : Civil-Military Co-operation in the Netherlands,
       <a href="/wiki/Cooperative_Cyber_Defence_Centre_of_Excellence" title="Cooperative Cyber Defence Centre of Excellence">
        Cooperative Cyber Defence
       </a>
       in Estonia and Energy Security in Lithuania. It plans to establish the NATO Strategic Communications Centre of Excellence in Riga.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
        <a href="#cite_note-134">
         [134]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Latvia co-operates with Estonia and Lithuania in several trilateral Baltic defence co-operation initiatives:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Baltic Battalion
        <i>
         (BALTBAT)
        </i>
        – infantry battalion for participation in international peace support operations, headquartered near
        <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">
         Riga
        </a>
        , Latvia;
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Naval_Squadron" title="Baltic Naval Squadron">
         Baltic Naval Squadron
        </a>
        <i>
         (BALTRON)
        </i>
        – naval force with mine countermeasures capabilities, headquartered near
        <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">
         Tallinn
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">
         Estonia
        </a>
        ;
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Air_Surveillance_Network" title="Baltic Air Surveillance Network">
         Baltic Air Surveillance Network
        </a>
        <i>
         (BALTNET)
        </i>
        – air surveillance information system, headquartered near
        <a href="/wiki/Kaunas" title="Kaunas">
         Kaunas
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">
         Lithuania
        </a>
        ;
       </li>
       <li>
        Joint military educational institutions:
        <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Defence_College" title="Baltic Defence College">
         Baltic Defence College
        </a>
        in
        <a href="/wiki/Tartu" title="Tartu">
         Tartu
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">
         Estonia
        </a>
        , Baltic Diving Training Centre in
        <a href="/wiki/Liep%C4%81ja" title="Liepāja">
         Liepāja
        </a>
        , Latvia and Baltic Naval Communications Training Centre in
        <a href="/wiki/Tallinn" title="Tallinn">
         Tallinn
        </a>
        , Estonia.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
         <a href="#cite_note-135">
          [135]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Future co-operation will include sharing of national infrastructures for training purposes and specialisation of training areas
       <i>
        (BALTTRAIN)
       </i>
       and collective formation of battalion-sized contingents for use in the NATO rapid-response force.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
        <a href="#cite_note-136">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In January 2011, the Baltic states were invited to join
       <a href="/wiki/NORDEFCO" title="NORDEFCO">
        NORDEFCO
       </a>
       , the defence framework of the
       <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">
        Nordic countries
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
        <a href="#cite_note-137">
         [137]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In November 2012, the three countries agreed to create a joint military staff in 2013.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
        <a href="#cite_note-138">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Latvia" title="Economy of Latvia">
        Economy of Latvia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BlueEurozone.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="690" data-file-width="645" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/220px-BlueEurozone.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/330px-BlueEurozone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/440px-BlueEurozone.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BlueEurozone.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Latvia is part of the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internal_market" title="Internal market">
          EU single market
         </a>
         (dark grey),
         <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">
          Eurozone
         </a>
         (dark blue) and
         <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">
          Schengen Area
         </a>
         (not shown).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Latvia is a member of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organisation" title="World Trade Organisation">
        World Trade Organisation
       </a>
       (1999) and the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       (2004). On 1 January 2014, the
       <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">
        Euro
       </a>
       became the country's currency, superseding the
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_lats" title="Latvian lats">
        Lats
       </a>
       . According to statistics in late 2013, 45% of the population supported the introduction of the euro, while 52% opposed it.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apollo.lv_139-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-apollo.lv-139">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Following the introduction of the Euro, Eurobarometer surveys in January 2014 showed support for the Euro to be around 53%, close to the European average.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
        <a href="#cite_note-140">
         [140]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Since the year 2000, Latvia has had one of the highest (GDP) growth rates in Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
        <a href="#cite_note-141">
         [141]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, the chiefly consumption-driven growth in Latvia resulted in the collapse of Latvian GDP in late 2008 and early 2009, exacerbated by the global economic crisis, shortage of credit and huge money resources used for the bailout of Parex bank.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
        <a href="#cite_note-142">
         [142]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Latvian economy fell 18% in the first three months of 2009, the biggest fall in the European Union.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
        <a href="#cite_note-143">
         [143]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
        <a href="#cite_note-144">
         [144]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lv_real_gdp_growth.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="867" data-file-width="1084" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Lv_real_gdp_growth.svg/220px-Lv_real_gdp_growth.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Lv_real_gdp_growth.svg/330px-Lv_real_gdp_growth.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Lv_real_gdp_growth.svg/440px-Lv_real_gdp_growth.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lv_real_gdp_growth.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Real GDP growth in Latvia 1996–2006
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The economic crisis of 2009 proved earlier assumptions that the fast-growing economy was heading for implosion of the
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_bubble" title="Economic bubble">
        economic bubble
       </a>
       , because it was driven mainly by growth of domestic
       <a href="/wiki/Consumption_(economics)" title="Consumption (economics)">
        consumption
       </a>
       , financed by a serious increase of private
       <a href="/wiki/Debt" title="Debt">
        debt
       </a>
       , as well as a negative foreign
       <a href="/wiki/Balance_of_trade" title="Balance of trade">
        trade balance
       </a>
       . The prices of real estate, which were at some points growing by approximately 5% a month, were long perceived to be too high for the economy, which mainly produces low-value goods and
       <a href="/wiki/Raw_material" title="Raw material">
        raw materials
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Privatisation" title="Privatisation">
        Privatisation
       </a>
       in Latvia is almost complete. Virtually all of the previously state-owned small and medium companies have been privatised, leaving only a small number of politically sensitive large state companies. The private sector accounted for nearly 68% of the country's GDP in 2000.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Foreign investment in Latvia is still modest compared with the levels in north-central Europe. A law expanding the scope for selling land, including to foreigners, was passed in 1997. Representing 10.2% of Latvia's total foreign direct investment, American companies invested $127 million in 1999. In the same year, the United States of America exported $58.2 million of goods and services to Latvia and imported $87.9 million. Eager to join Western economic institutions like the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organisation" title="World Trade Organisation">
        World Trade Organisation
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">
        OECD
       </a>
       , and the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       , Latvia signed a Europe Agreement with the EU in 1995—with a 4-year transition period. Latvia and the United States have signed treaties on investment, trade, and intellectual property protection and avoidance of double taxation.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Economic_contraction_and_recovery_.282008.E2.80.9312.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_contraction_and_recovery_(2008–12)">
        Economic contraction and recovery (2008–12)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Economic contraction and recovery (2008–12)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%932010_Latvian_financial_crisis" title="2008–2010 Latvian financial crisis">
        2008–2010 Latvian financial crisis
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AirBaltic_Boeing_757-200_at_RIX.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/AirBaltic_Boeing_757-200_at_RIX.jpg/220px-AirBaltic_Boeing_757-200_at_RIX.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/AirBaltic_Boeing_757-200_at_RIX.jpg/330px-AirBaltic_Boeing_757-200_at_RIX.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/AirBaltic_Boeing_757-200_at_RIX.jpg/440px-AirBaltic_Boeing_757-200_at_RIX.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AirBaltic_Boeing_757-200_at_RIX.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         An
         <a href="/wiki/AirBaltic" title="AirBaltic">
          airBaltic
         </a>
         Boeing 757−200WL takes off at
         <a href="/wiki/Riga_International_Airport" title="Riga International Airport">
          Riga International Airport
         </a>
         (RIX)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Latvian economy entered a phase of fiscal contraction during the second half of 2008 after an extended period of credit-based speculation and unrealistic appreciation in real estate values. The national account deficit for 2007, for example, represented more than 22% of the GDP for the year while inflation was running at 10%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_145-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-145">
         [145]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Latvia's unemployment rate rose sharply in this period from a low of 5.4% in November 2007 to over 22%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
        <a href="#cite_note-146">
         [146]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In April 2010 Latvia had the highest unemployment rate in the EU, at 22.5%, ahead of Spain, which had 19.7%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
        <a href="#cite_note-147">
         [147]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Paul_Krugman" title="Paul Krugman">
        Paul Krugman
       </a>
       , the Nobel Laureate in economics for 2008, wrote in his
       <a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">
        New York Times
       </a>
       Op-Ed column on 15 December 2008:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        "The most acute problems are on Europe's periphery, where many smaller economies are experiencing crises strongly reminiscent of past crises in Latin America and Asia: Latvia is the new Argentina "
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
         <a href="#cite_note-148">
          [148]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       However, by 2010, commentators
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economist_149-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-economist-149">
         [149]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-XE_150-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-XE-150">
         [150]
        </a>
       </sup>
       noted signs of stabilisation in the Latvian economy. Rating agency
       <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor's">
        Standard &amp; Poor's
       </a>
       raised its outlook on Latvia's debt from negative to stable.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economist_149-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-economist-149">
         [149]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Latvia's current account, which had been in deficit by 27% in late 2006 was in surplus in February 2010.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economist_149-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-economist-149">
         [149]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Kenneth Orchard, senior analyst at
       <a href="/wiki/Moody%27s_Investors_Service" title="Moody's Investors Service">
        Moody's Investors Service
       </a>
       argued that:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        "The strengthening regional economy is supporting Latvian production and exports, while the sharp swing in the current account balance suggests that the country's ‘internal devaluation’ is working."
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">
         <a href="#cite_note-151">
          [151]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IMF" title="IMF">
        IMF
       </a>
       concluded the First Post-Program Monitoring Discussions with the Republic of Latvia in July 2012 announcing that Latvia's economy has been recovering strongly since 2010, following the deep downturn in 2008–09. Real GDP growth of 5.5 percent in 2011 was underpinned by export growth and a recovery in domestic demand. The growth momentum has continued into 2012 and 2013 despite deteriorating external conditions, and the economy is expected to expand by 4.1 percent in 2014. The unemployment rate has receded from its peak of more than 20 percent in 2010 to around 9.3 percent in 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">
        <a href="#cite_note-152">
         [152]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">
        Infrastructure
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ventspils_osta.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="446" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Ventspils_osta.jpg/220px-Ventspils_osta.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Ventspils_osta.jpg/330px-Ventspils_osta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Ventspils_osta.jpg/440px-Ventspils_osta.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ventspils_osta.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_port_of_Ventspils" title="Free port of Ventspils">
          Port of Ventspils
         </a>
         is one of the busiest ports in the
         <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">
          Baltic states
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Latvia" title="Transport in Latvia">
        Transport in Latvia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The transport sector is around 14% of GDP. Transit between Russia, Belarus, Kazakhstan as well as other Asian countries and the West is large.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wpt_153-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-wpt-153">
         [153]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The three biggest ports of Latvia are located in
       <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">
        Riga
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ventspils" title="Ventspils">
        Ventspils
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Liep%C4%81ja" title="Liepāja">
        Liepāja
       </a>
       . Most transit traffic uses these and half the cargo is crude oil and oil products.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wpt_153-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-wpt-153">
         [153]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_port_of_Ventspils" title="Free port of Ventspils">
        Free port of Ventspils
       </a>
       is one of the busiest ports in the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">
        Baltic states
       </a>
       . Apart from road and railway connections, Ventspils is also linked to oil extraction fields and transportation routes of Russian Federation via system of two pipelines from
       <a href="/wiki/Polotsk" title="Polotsk">
        Polotsk
       </a>
       , Belarus.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Riga_International_Airport" title="Riga International Airport">
        Riga International Airport
       </a>
       is the busiest airport in the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">
        Baltic states
       </a>
       with 4.7 million passengers in 2012. It has direct flight to over 80 destinations in 30 countries.
       <a href="/wiki/AirBaltic" title="AirBaltic">
        airBaltic
       </a>
       is the Latvian flag carrier airline and a low-cost carrier.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Latvia has three big hydroelectric power stations in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P%C4%BCavi%C5%86u_HES" title="Pļaviņu HES">
        Pļaviņu HES
       </a>
       (825MW),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%C4%ABgas_HES" title="Rīgas HES">
        Rīgas HES
       </a>
       (402 MW) and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C4%B6eguma_HES-2" title="Ķeguma HES-2">
        Ķeguma HES-2
       </a>
       (192 MW). In the recent years a couple of dozen of wind farms as well as biogas or biomass power stations of different scale have been built in Latvia.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Latvia operates
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=In%C4%8Dukalns_underground_gas_storage_facility&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Inčukalns underground gas storage facility (page does not exist)">
        Inčukalns underground gas storage facility
       </a>
       , one of the largest
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_storage" title="Natural gas storage">
        underground gas storage facilities
       </a>
       in Europe and the only one in the Baltic states. Unique geological conditions at Inčukalns and other locations in Latvia are particularly suitable for underground gas storage.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">
        <a href="#cite_note-154">
         [154]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Latvia" title="Demographics of Latvia">
        Demographics of Latvia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
        <table style="border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">
         <tr style="background:none">

           Residents of Latvia by ethnicity (2011)
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nat_1-1">

            </a>
           </sup>
          </th>
         </tr>
         <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">

          </td>
          <td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;">
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           Latvians
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:DarkSlateGray; width:62.1%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           62.1%
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           Russians
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:DarkSlateGray; width:26.9%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           26.9%
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           Belarusians
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:DarkSlateGray; width:3.3%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>
          </td>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">
           3.3%
          </td>
         </tr>
         <tr>
          <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">
           Ukrainians
          </td>
          <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
           <div style="background:DarkSlateGray; width:2.2%; overflow: hidden;">
           </div>

           2.2%
          </td>

           2.2%
          </td>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Population-of-Latvia.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2205" data-file-width="3119" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Population-of-Latvia.svg/300px-Population-of-Latvia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Population-of-Latvia.svg/450px-Population-of-Latvia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Population-of-Latvia.svg/600px-Population-of-Latvia.svg.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Population-of-Latvia.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Population of Latvia (in millions) from 1920 to 2014
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">
        total fertility rate
       </a>
       (TFR) in 2013 was estimated at 1.52 children born/woman, which is lower than the replacement rate of 2.1. In 2012, 45.0% of births were to unmarried women.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">
        <a href="#cite_note-155">
         [155]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The life expectancy in 2013 was estimated at 73.19 years (68.13 years male, 78.53 years female).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_145-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-145">
         [145]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of 2015, Latvia is estimated to have the lowest male-to-female ratio in total population, at 0.85 males/female.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">
        <a href="#cite_note-156">
         [156]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">
        Ethnic groups
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latvian_people" title="Latvian people">
        Latvian people
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_Latvia" title="Russians in Latvia">
        Latvian Russians
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latvian_Germans" title="Latvian Germans">
        Latvian Germans
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latvian_Jews" title="Latvian Jews">
        Latvian Jews
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latgalians_(modern)" title="Latgalians (modern)">
        Latgalians (modern)
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Livonians" title="Livonians">
        Livonians
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Gauja_Estonians" title="Gauja Estonians">
        Gauja Estonians
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Latvia's population has been
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiethnic_society" title="Multiethnic society">
        multiethnic
       </a>
       for centuries, though the demographics shifted dramatically in the 20th century due to the World Wars, the emigration and removal of
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Germans" title="Baltic Germans">
        Baltic Germans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">
        the Holocaust
       </a>
       , and occupation by the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
        Soviet Union
       </a>
       . According to the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire_Census" title="Russian Empire Census">
        Russian Empire Census
       </a>
       of 1897, Latvians formed 68.3% of the total population of 1.93 million; Russians accounted for 12%, Jews for 7.4%, Germans for 6.2%, and Poles for 3.4%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">
        <a href="#cite_note-157">
         [157]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As of March 2011,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latvian_people" title="Latvian people">
        Latvians
       </a>
       form about 62.1% of the population, while 26.9% are
       <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_the_Baltic_states" title="Russians in the Baltic states">
        Russians
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">
        Belarusians
       </a>
       3.3%,
       <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">
        Ukrainians
       </a>
       2.2%,
       <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">
        Poles
       </a>
       2.2%,
       <a href="/wiki/Lithuanians" title="Lithuanians">
        Lithuanians
       </a>
       1.2%,
       <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">
        Jews
       </a>
       0.3%,
       <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">
        Romani people
       </a>
       0.3%,
       <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">
        Germans
       </a>
       0.1%,
       <a href="/wiki/Estonians" title="Estonians">
        Estonians
       </a>
       0.1% and others 1.3%. 250 people identify as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Livonian_people" title="Livonian people">
        Livonians
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Finns" title="Baltic Finns">
        Baltic Finnic
       </a>
       people native to Latvia). There were 290,660
       <a href="/wiki/Non-citizens_(Latvia)" title="Non-citizens (Latvia)">
        non-citizens
       </a>
       living in Latvia or 14.1% of Latvian residents, mainly ethnic Russians who arrived after the occupation of 1940 and their descendants.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">
        <a href="#cite_note-158">
         [158]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In some cities, e.g.,
       <a href="/wiki/Daugavpils" title="Daugavpils">
        Daugavpils
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/R%C4%93zekne" title="Rēzekne">
        Rēzekne
       </a>
       , ethnic Latvians constitute a minority of the total population. Despite the fact that the proportion of ethnic Latvians has been steadily increasing for more than a decade, ethnic Latvians also make up slightly less than a half of the population of the capital city of Latvia –
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%C4%ABga" title="Rīga">
        Rīga
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">
        <a href="#cite_note-159">
         [159]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The share of ethnic Latvians had fallen from 77% (1,467,035) in 1935 to 52% (1,387,757) in 1989.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">
        <a href="#cite_note-160">
         [160]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2011, there were even fewer Latvians than in 1989, though their share of the population was larger – 1,285,136 (62.1% of the population).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">
        <a href="#cite_note-161">
         [161]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Language">
        Language
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Language">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Language_policy_in_Latvia" title="Language policy in Latvia">
        Language policy in Latvia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The sole official language of Latvia is
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">
        Latvian
       </a>
       , which belongs to the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_languages" title="Baltic languages">
        Baltic language sub-group
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Balto-Slavic_languages" title="Balto-Slavic languages">
        Balto-Slavic branch
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">
        Indo-European language family
       </a>
       . Another notable language of Latvia is the nearly extinct
       <a href="/wiki/Livonian_language" title="Livonian language">
        Livonian language
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Finnic_languages" title="Finnic languages">
        Finnic
       </a>
       branch of the
       <a href="/wiki/Uralic_languages" title="Uralic languages">
        Uralic language family
       </a>
       , which enjoys protection by law;
       <a href="/wiki/Latgalian_language" title="Latgalian language">
        Latgalian
       </a>
       – referred to as either a dialect or a distinct separate language of Latvian – is also formally protected by Latvian law but only as a historical variation of the Latvian language. Russian, which was widely spoken during the Soviet period, is still the most widely used minority language by far (about 34% speak it at home, including people who are not ethnically Russian).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">
        <a href="#cite_note-162">
         [162]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While it is now required that all school students learn Latvian, most schools also include English and either German or Russian in their curricula. English is widely accepted in Latvia, especially in business and tourism. As of 2014
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       there are 109 schools for minorities that use Russian as the language of instruction for 40% of subjects (the rest 60% of subjects are taught in Latvian).
      </p>
      <p>
       On 18 February 2012, Latvia held a
       <a href="/wiki/Latvian_constitutional_referendum,_2012" title="Latvian constitutional referendum, 2012">
        constitutional referendum
       </a>
       on whether to adopt Russian as a second official language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">
        <a href="#cite_note-163">
         [163]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to the Central Election Commission, 74.8% voted against, 24.9% voted for and the voter turnout was 71.1%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">
        <a href="#cite_note-164">
         [164]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [

         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Latvia" title="Religion in Latvia">
        Religion in Latvia
       </a>
      </div>

           </div>
